Amidst the Economic Downturn: Yongxingzhuang Ceases Business Yesterday; Has Entrusted a Lawyer to Announce Liquidation 98

According to the Central News Agency, another new example of the economic downturn in this city occurred yesterday, namely the Yongxing Huihua Zhuang at No. 11 Xingren Lane, 120 Ningbo Road, which also ceased business. As the end of April closing period is approaching, this phenomenon was also expected. The Central News Agency reporter learned of the following details yesterday:

History of Establishment

Yongxingzhuang was established in February of the 20th year of the Republic of China, with a capital of 300,000 yuan, divided into ten shares. The shareholders were Chen Dizhou (three shares), Yu Zhendong (two and a half shares), Guo Ruoyu (two shares), Chen Zhongchi (one and a half shares), and Chen Meibai (one share). The manager was Chen Jingtao, the assistant manager was Wang Hanqing, and the assistant manager was Chen Dizhou. The business involved remittances and loans. Although it was not established for long, its creditworthiness was quite remarkable.

Announcement of Liquidation

The previous night, due to the failure to deliver 70,000 yuan in remittances, it was forced to announce its closure at 10:00 PM that night. From yesterday morning, it did not open for business. Manager Chen Jingtao entrusted lawyer Xu Zuyan to announce liquidation. Important staff members have not been going to the Zhuang to work since that day. Only a few trainees remained inside to take care of things.

Reasons for Closure

The Central News Agency reporter interviewed Xu Zuyan, the liquidator of the Zhuang, yesterday. According to him, the Zhuang's accounts have been mostly reviewed. In addition to the capital of 300,000 yuan, there were over 900,000 yuan in deposits and 700,000-800,000 yuan in loans. Assets and liabilities are roughly equal. The reason for the forced closure this time is nothing more than the impact of the economic downturn. Yongxingzhuang invested heavily in real estate mortgages. Some mortgages have expired and been taken over by the Zhuang, but they cannot be sold, leading to stagnation. However, the losses to creditors should not be too significant, only a matter of time. As for the question of whether it can resume business, a Qianzhuang is not comparable to a bank. Its establishment relies solely on credit. Once it closes, it is difficult to have hope of recovery.

Lawyer's Notice

Lawyer Xu Zuyan, representing Yongxing Qianzhuang, announced a liquidation notice, stating: "According to the agent of Yongxing Qianzhuang, the Zhuang has been affected by the sluggish market, resulting in poor turnover, and has had to suspend business and announce liquidation. Please make a public announcement, handle registration procedures, and recover outstanding debts. Therefore, this announcement is made on behalf of the agent. All creditors of the Zhuang must, within fourteen days from today, register at this firm with their debt instruments. All debtors must also pay off their debts in full within the above-mentioned period. Failure to do so will result in legal action. Do not delay. Lawyer Xu Zuyan, April 21st, 24th year of the Republic of China, Office: Room 406, Xingye Building, Beijing Road Intersection, Shanghai, Telephone: 19074."

Art Exhibition: Preview Day 14 101

Yesterday (the 21st) was the 14th day of the Shanghai preview of the International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London. Since its opening, it has been two weeks, and the average daily number of visitors has been around 2,000. Yesterday was a Sunday, a regular holiday for various organizations, so the number of visitors was even more crowded. The entrance to the venue was bustling with activity. Here is a summary of the news obtained yesterday:

Visits by Celebrities in Recent Days

In the past two days, celebrities who visited the exhibition included Cai Yuanpei, President of the Academia Sinica; Chu Minyi, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan; Xu Beihong, professor and artist of Central University; Li Ximou, Dean of Studies of Jinan University; He DeKui, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Council. Hu Shi, Dean of the Faculty of Arts of Peking University, will also visit the exhibition with American educator Paul Monroe. Recently, a delegation from an American economic survey group also intends to visit the exhibition.

More Antiquities Arrive

A total of 100 pieces of Yin oracle bones, stone knives, stone axes, bronze molds, ivory carvings, etc., previously sent by the Academia Sinica for exhibition, have been displayed in the seventh room. However, the Academia Sinica plans to send more of these antiquities. It is said that they will arrive next Wednesday (the 24th).

Trends in the Evolution of Painting

The second chapter of the explanation of calligraphy and painting written by the exhibition, "The Evolution of Calligraphy and its Masters," was published in yesterday's newspaper. Here is the third chapter, "The Lack of Evolution of Calligraphy and its Learning," and its famous scholars, continued for reference by those who study calligraphy and painting. To the utmost of learning's complexity, it is divided into three categories: landscape, figures, and sketches, and explained as follows: (1) Specializing in landscape painting originated in the Six Dynasties and flourished in the Tang Dynasty. For convenience of explanation, it can be divided into the Northern and Southern Schools. The Southern School takes gentleness to capture charm, gaining ethereal spirit from the tangible, emphasizing brushwork. The Northern School takes strength to capture momentum, revealing real power from the intangible, emphasizing the use of condensation. Wang Wei is regarded as the ancestor of the Southern School, with Yang Sheng and Lu Hong of the Tang Dynasty, Jing Hao, Guan Quan, Dong Yuan, and Ju Ran of the Five Dynasties, Li Cheng, Fan Kuan, Hui Chong, Yan Wengui, Xu Daoning, Guo Xi, Zhao Danian, Mi Fu, Jiang Can, Mi Youren of the Song Dynasty, Zhao Mengfu, Qian Xuan, Gao Kegong, Huang Gongwang, Cao Zhibai, Wu Zhen, Wang Meng, Ni Zan, Sheng Mao, Zhu Derun, Tang Di, Chen Ruyan, and Xu Ben of the Yuan Dynasty, Wang Hong, Liu Yu, Shen Zhou, Wen Zhengming, and Dong Qichang of the Ming Dynasty, and Wang Shimin, Wang Jian, Wang Hui, Wang Yuanqi, Wu Li, Yun Shouping, Shi Xi, Shi Tao, Bada Shanren, Emperor Gaozong, Tang Yifen, and Dai Xi of the Qing Dynasty inheriting the Dharma milk, without interruption for over a thousand years. Northern School landscapes often combine figures and buildings, with both meticulous and raw styles. Li Sixun and Li Zhaodao of the Tang Dynasty, known as the Big and Small Generals Li, are their representatives. The meticulous style of the Northern School includes Wang Xi, Zhao Zonghan, Zhao Boju, Zhao Boxiu, and Liu Songnian of the Song Dynasty, Ge Ziping, Wang Zhenpeng of the Yuan Dynasty, and Qiu Ying and Wu Bin of the Ming Dynasty as one line. The raw style includes Li Tang, Zhu Rui, Ma Yuan, and Xia Gui of the Song Dynasty, Liu Guandao of the Yuan Dynasty, and Dai Jin, Kai Chen, Tang Yin, and Lan Ying of the Ming Dynasty as one line. Early Qing painting styles still followed the late Ming style, such as Wang Duo, Zai Mingshuo, Fu Shan, and Fa Ruozhen, who were all close to the Northern School. These two schools sometimes mixed with each other and were not strictly divided. Observers should be good at distinguishing them. (2) Figure painting probably began in the Han Dynasty, continued through the Six Dynasties, and was slightly influenced by foreign influences. The works handed down from the Tang Dynasty are more reliable. Yan Liben, Wu Daozi, the Big and Small Weichi, and Zhou Fang of the Tang Dynasty, Zhou Wenju and Qiu Wenbo of the Five Dynasties, Shi Ke, Chao Guangjiu, Li Boshi, Su Hanchen, Ma Hezhi, Zhang Zeduan, Jia Shigu, Liang Kai, and Li Song of the Song Dynasty, Zhao Mengfu, Zhao Yong, Zhao Yanzheng, and the Zu Sun family of the Yuan Dynasty, and Wu Wei, Guo Xu, Du Jin, Tang Yin, Qiu Ying, Ding Yunpeng, and Cui Zizhong of the Ming Dynasty, and Chen Hongshou, Zhang Feng, Hua Yan, and Gai Qi of the Qing Dynasty, either wrote facts or captured charm, combining meticulous and freehand styles, each with their own strengths. (3) For sketches, Han Gan, Dai Song, Han Huang, Bian Luan, and Diao Guangyin of the Tang Dynasty, Xu Xi, Huang Quan, and Teng Changyou of the Five Dynasties, and Huang Quan's son Ju Cai, Xu Xi's grandson Chongsi, each with their own family traditions, Zhao Chang, Cui Bai, Ai Xuan, Wu Yuanyu, Lin Chun, Wu Bingli, Di, and Ma Lin of the Song Dynasty, Lu Zonggui, Xiao Rong of the Liao Dynasty, Qian Xuan, Wang Yuanming, Emperor Xuanzong of the Ming Dynasty, Lin Liang, Lu Ji, Lu Zhi, Chen Daofu, Wang Guxiang, Xu Wei, Zhou Zhimian, and Chen Kuo of the Ming Dynasty, and Yun Shouping, Wang Wu, Jin Nong, Jiang Tingxi, and Zou Yigui of the Qing Dynasty all had their own specialties. This school of painting, in its meticulousness, still possesses charm. Its coloring and transmission of colors are extremely refined. Among them, there is also a freehand style, which is good at using reduced brushstrokes, with few strokes but sufficient expression, not flowing into wildness, far surpassing general court books that only imitate.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Writes to the Bureau of Public Works Requesting the Opening of the Tongmatang Dam 108

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce wrote to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works yesterday, stating: "To whom it may concern, according to a letter from Zhong Yibo, director of the Jiangwan branch of our chamber, dated the 19th of this month, the Zoumatang River in this town has not been opened, affecting the transportation of goods and causing great suffering to merchants. According to this, we found that on the 4th of this month, the branch office sent a letter with the same request, and we sent a letter to your bureau with No. 393, requesting that you expedite the matter. Now it is said that the entire river project will take time to complete and accept. Long-term enclosure of the dam is indeed detrimental to the transportation of goods. We are sending this letter for your attention, hoping that your bureau will approve the request in the previous letter and order the dam to be opened at both the east and west ends, while ordering the river dredging project to be completed as soon as possible, in order to facilitate traffic. We look forward to your reply, and we are deeply grateful."

Large Number of Fishermen from Wenzhou Arrive in Shanghai; Fellow-Provincials Association Finds Ways to Provide Relief 110

According to the New Voice News Agency, more than 300 fishermen from Wenzhou, including Zhou Zhiming, found it difficult to make a living in their hometown and brought their fishing gear to fish in the Huawushan and Shengshan areas of Chongming County. On the 12th of this month, they took the Fuping steamboat of the Zhenan Company from Ruian and Pingyang to Huawushan and Shengshan. Unexpectedly, when they arrived, they were refused landing by the local fishermen, who even fired shots as a warning. Zhou Zhiming and others, fearing trouble, took the boat back to Shanghai, arriving the day before yesterday. The boat docked at the Nanmatou of Shiliupu. Representatives were sent to the Wenzhou Fellow-Provincials Association to request relief. After receiving the report, the association found that the fishermen had limited funds, could not afford to stay in hotels, and had no place to stay due to the large number of people. Therefore, it ordered them to stay on the boat temporarily and sent letters to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Water Patrol Team for protection to avoid trouble. At the same time, it also requested the Shanghai Ping Steamboat Joint Bureau to reduce fares for the fishermen and send them back to their hometown.

From 7:00 AM to 5:00 PM every day, six round trips will be made, with each trip taking one and a half hours. The route is divided into two sections: (1) From Shanghai to Luodian, with a branch line to Liuhe Xinzhai; (2) From Shanghai to Luodian, with a branch line to the east gate of Jiading city. It is reported that the company will hold an opening ceremony when it moves into the new site to invite people from all walks of life to visit.

Second Group Wedding: Machine Industry Association Distributes "The Way of Husband and Wife" 113

The Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factories Association, in order to promote conjugal love, specially sent a letter to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, requesting that "The Way of Husband and Wife" be distributed when the second group wedding of the new life movement is held on May 1st. The original letter stated: "To whom it may concern, the way of husband and wife is profound and complex. In ancient times, some people disliked their wives being naked in private rooms, while others loved their wives so much that they forgot their status. Because of the difference between love and dislike, some were as intimate as mandarin ducks, while others separated like swallows. Since the eastward spread of Europeanization, freedom has been valued, and the Zhou Dynasty's influence is no longer heard of in today's world. The matter of breaking free from constraints is even more frequently reported in newspapers. Husband and wife are the starting point of human relations. If the way of husband and wife is bitter, the family will be in turmoil. The association has recognized this and has published an article on "The Way of Husband and Wife" in each issue of the Machine Industry Association Journal in the past, so as to guide the young couples of the 20th century onto the right track, so that they can enjoy the harmony of the zither and the flute, and the love in the boudoir is more important than everything else. It has now been published as a separate book entitled "The Way of Husband and Wife." We have learned that your bureau has scheduled to hold the second group wedding ceremony of the new life movement at the Municipal Government Auditorium on May 1st, eliminating cumbersome procedures and reforming bad customs, and forging a marriage alliance, which is indeed a grand event for promoting the new life movement. However, the way of husband and wife cannot be absent to embellish it. Our association intends to send some copies at that time for your bureau to give to the newlyweds, so that they can have a good relationship and grow old together. Perhaps it will also be an aid to the government's promotion of the new life movement. We hereby send this letter and await your reply."

Investigation of Trafficking in Young Girls 115

Yin Wang, a woman from Taizhou residing at No. 44, Sanqingfang, Huade Road, had a daughter named Liu Mei, 13 years old. Due to poverty, it was difficult to make a living. On March 18th, at about 3:00 PM, Wang Mama, an old woman from the same village, and Chen Liji, from Yangzhou, introduced her to Wu Ziheng and his wife Qiao, from the same village at No. 72, Lane 142, Xinji Bang Road, as a maid. It was agreed that the annual salary would be four yuan, for a period of two years. The girl was sent to work for several months. The girl's mother went to Chen to get the four yuan, asking him to pass on the message. Chen made excuses to negotiate, but never returned. The next day, Xiang said that Wu Ziheng's family had moved and could not be found. Yin Wang realized that these people had colluded to sell her daughter and turned them over to Hua Police Officer No. 1741 and Detective Ji Xiucheng, who took them to the Yangshupu Police Station. The police chief learned the details and ordered them to be detained. The day before yesterday at noon, Detective Ji learned from a mover named Xi that Wu Ziheng and his wife were hiding at the home of a friend at No. 60 in the same lane. He secretly went to the address and arrested Wang and others. Yesterday, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, detailed the previous situation and said that the defendants had said in the police station that Zhao Zhiming, who was at large, had taken the girl to Daqiao and sold her for forty yuan, which was shared and used. The case was requested to be postponed. Then, Wang's mother proved the process. When questioned, the defendants' statements were vague. Judge Wu Zehan ordered them to be detained separately for further verification at a later date.

Ministry of Judicial Administration Negotiates the Case of Cui Yingxin's Arrest; Refers It to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for Investigation and Handling 117

Cui Yingxin (formerly Li Mingyu), who naturalized in our country on June 13, 1925, was arrested by the French police at his residence in Xiechengli, Laoshenfu Road, Shanghai on March 26 of this year and handed over to the Japanese Consulate for illegal detention. The case of the confiscation of his naturalization certificate on the spot has been delegated by Cui Yingxin's wife to lawyers Lou Yunmei and Xu Jie to negotiate with the French police and the French Consul General in Shanghai. At the same time, telegrams were sent to the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Judicial Administration, requesting that legal rights be upheld and a serious protest be lodged. On the 17th of this month, lawyers Lou Yunmei and Xu Jie received document No. 1111 from the Ministry of Judicial Administration, which stated that the applicant, Lou Yunmei, etc., had sent a telegram on behalf of Cui Yingxin, who had naturalized in our country, that Cui Yingxin had been illegally detained by the French police and handed over to the Japanese Consulate, requesting that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs be consulted. The telegram has been forwarded to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for investigation and handling. This document was issued on April 16, 24th year of the Republic of China, by Wang Yongbin, Minister of the Ministry of Judicial Administration.

Illegally Setting Up a Morphine Factory; Accomplice Russian Arrested; Russian Vigorously Denies; Order to Retrieve Case Files for Further Interrogation 119

A Russian named Artemski, Si Dani Sila (transliteration), 45 years old this year, invested 4,000 yuan in January 1933 to partner with a Frenchman named Aiju Bo Liye (transliteration) and a German named Bai Shi (transliteration) to open a morphine factory in the Chinese area of ​​West Shanghai, Columbia Road. Bai Shi was hired as a secretly manufacturing engineer. Before long, the competent public security bureau found out and arrested the German Bai Shi and hired Chinese accomplices Zhang Yunbao and Jin A'gen, and confiscated machines and toxic substances. They were transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for trial. Bai Shi was sentenced to one year in prison and fined 3,000 yuan. The Chinese Zhang Yunbao and others were also sentenced separately. The Frenchman Aiju Bo Liye was also arrested and transferred to the French Consulate for interrogation. He was sentenced to one year in prison and fined 3,000 francs on February 7 of that year. Aiju refused to accept the original verdict and appealed to the High Court of Saigon, Annam. At that time, the Russian Artemski was the only one who escaped and lived freely until now. Two years later, at the beginning of this year, the German Bai Shi was released after serving his sentence and paying a fine by the Shanghai Local Court. Because the Russian Artemski was also a shareholder, he did not provide assistance or rescue at the time. It was hateful to be free. Because he lived at No. 35, No. 66 Laerdong Road in the French Concession, he reported it to the French police, requesting an arrest and interrogation. The chief of police approved and sent detectives to arrest Artemski on March 6 this year and found the correspondence between Aiju Bo Liye and Bai Shi and evidence that he sold toxic substances. He was taken back to the police station for detention and transferred to the First Special District Local Court. The police lawyer filed a public prosecution based on the Anti-Smoking Law and the Criminal Law. Judge Zhang Chaozuo opened several court sessions for interrogation. The defendant denied colluding to open a morphine factory. He was ordered to be remanded in custody for a later date to retrieve and review the case file of Aiju Bo Liye from the French Consulate before conducting another interrogation. The judge opened another court session the day before yesterday for further interrogation. Lawyer Gu Shouxi from the police department appeared in court. Bai Shi, the witness who was summoned, did not arrive. When asked, the defendant still denied it. The court verified the confession and, since the summoned witness had not arrived and the French Consulate case file was still in the Saigon Court and had not been retrieved, it was ruled that the defendant should be remanded to the police station for another interrogation at a later date.

Lingzhi Appears; An Ancient Auspicious Herb, Highly Precious; Tourists Compete to Visit; Displayed at the Municipal Botanical Garden 121

The Municipal Botanical Garden on Longhua Road in this port has been established for more than half a year, and its equipment and layout are considered perfect. It has spared no effort in searching for plant varieties on weekdays. Recently, it sought a plant of purple lingzhi from Xu Keming, a scientific and industrial designer, and displayed it in the exhibition hall, which is very precious. The shape of the lingzhi is like a mushroom. The top of the cap has cloud patterns and is purplish-brown. The bottom is light brown with fine pores. The stem is purplish-red. Its texture is hard and smooth, and the whole shape is complete. According to ancient records, there are six colors of lingzhi: blue, red, yellow, white, black, and purple. It was regarded as an auspicious herb in ancient times, so it is called lingzhi, also known as purple lingzhi. It is said that the number of tourists has increased sharply in recent days, and they all want to see the lingzhi to feast their eyes.

This is heartbreaking. It is all because adults, gentlemen, ladies, and misses are fond of fashion and Western products, wearing suits and leather shoes. They have completely forgotten the sounds of gunfire on September 18th and January 28th, using precious money to provide foreigners with the means to manufacture guns and cannons to slaughter our compatriots. This is a heartbreaking matter. Although this is a manifestation of treacherous merchants loving money and forgetting the nation, it is also the result of compatriots being greedy for cheap goods. Even more strange is that people who wear Western clothes, eat Western food, and ride in cars constantly shout about promoting national products, without thinking about their own clothing, food, housing, and transportation. All of this is a contradictory phenomenon. He hoped that from this year onward, all Chinese people would unite as one, block the outflow of money, promote national products, and boycott foreign goods, so that the country can be revived.

Awards Presentation

Finally, the children performed songs, Cantonese opera, Peking opera, and other performances. Then, the awards ceremony was held. The 24 winners were: 1. Ding Zixiao, 2. Du Jie, 3. Fang Meili, 4. Ma Sihong, 5. Qian Jingyun, 6. Zhou Qichang, 7. Xu Guanglin, 8. Cheng Shufang, 9. Xu Si, 10. Liu Ruonan, 11. Qin Pengzhang, 12. Chen Rong, 13. Chen Tianle, 14. Xu Weishan, 15. Du Daqi, 16. Tragic Boating Accident at Liwa Lita Village: Chen Siblings Tragically Die, Village Authorities Should Improve Conditions Immediately 132

Chen Wenlan, a 32-year-old man from Dinghai, took his cousin Chen Xiufeng (also known as Ding Chenshi), 29 years old, and other relatives, nine people in total, to Liwa Lita Village in West Shanghai for a holiday outing yesterday afternoon at 3 PM. After walking around for a while, Chen and his relatives decided to go boating. They split into two groups and took two small boats to go boating on the river. Chen and his cousin, along with three others, were in one boat, leading the way. The other four people were in another small boat, following behind. Unexpectedly, when Chen's boat reached the middle of the river, it suddenly tilted to the left due to uneven weight distribution. The people in the boat panicked and, in the chaos, the boat capsized, causing everyone to fall into the water. Chen's relatives in the boat behind saw this and bravely rowed over to rescue them. They saw three people clinging to the side of the boat and rescued them first. However, Chen and Xiufeng were nowhere to be seen. After pushing the overturned boat aside, Chen and Xiufeng were finally brought out of the water. The village staff had also heard the news and rushed to the scene, quickly pulling up Chen and Ding Chenshi. However, they had swallowed too much water, and their faces were lifeless, with only a faint breath remaining. They were rushed to Hong'en Hospital for treatment, but despite the hospital administering oxygen and other treatments, it was ineffective, and they soon died. The bodies were taken by their relatives to the Huanqiu Funeral Home on Jing'an Temple Road, and the coffin was scheduled for placement on the afternoon of the 23rd, a truly tragic event. However, after investigation, this is not the first accident involving boating in this village. The reason for the accidents may be that the construction of the small boats is not adequate. It is hoped that the village staff will quickly improve the situation to avoid future tragedies.

Yesterday was Easter Sunday: Believers Celebrated in Unison, Catholics Held High Mass, Christians Held Enlarged Services 133

Yesterday was Easter Sunday (the resurrection of Jesus Christ), and believers of all faiths, both Chinese and foreign, celebrated in unison. Catholic believers held High Mass, and Christian believers held Easter services. Foreign banks also closed for three days, starting on the 19th, to show their celebration. At the same time, telegram offices transmitted social telegrams, totaling over 500 throughout the day. Details are as follows:

Catholic Believers: High Mass

Yesterday, Catholic believers were busy holding the great feast of the resurrection of Jesus from morning to night. Starting at 5 AM, High Mass was held at the Catholic Church on Yong'an Street. The church authorities had decorated the inside and outside of the church with evergreen branches, cypress branches, and colorful flags. At 5 AM, Father Shan Lijiassa led the choir, students, and Chinese and foreign believers in the service. At 10 AM, the Easter High Mass was held. After reciting the scriptures at 11 AM, people gradually left. Over 5,000 Chinese and foreign believers participated, including the French Consul General in Shanghai. At 3 PM in the afternoon, the Blessed Sacrament Easter service was held. At 4 PM, the Blessed Sacrament Benediction service was held. At 7:30 PM, after Mass, the Blessed Sacrament was displayed, and over 3,000 believers attended.

20,000 Participants from Afar

The church was decorated solemnly. Believers who participated all bowed and worshiped. White lights and cloth banners were lit in front of Jesus. At the same time, High Mass was also held at major churches in Xujiahui, Dongjiadu, Hongkou, and Datong Road. The total number of participants reached 20,000. Catholics from as far as Suzhou, Songjiang, and the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways also came to Shanghai to participate. The scene was very enthusiastic.

Christian Believers: Enlarged Services

Yesterday, Christian believers also held enlarged services. From 10:40 AM to 11:00 AM, services were held separately at Moore Memorial Church, Haige Road, and the German Educational Road Xiren Church. At 4 PM in the afternoon, the Shanghai YMCA celebrated the Christian Resurrection Movement at the auditorium of the new YMCA building at Baxianqiao, and a musical worship service was held. Wu Yaozong spoke on "The True Meaning of Christ's Resurrection," and the Guangdong Chinese Christian Church Sacred Music Troupe performed. The program included: (1) Music, (2) Hymn (congregation standing together to sing) "The Lord is Risen," (3) AlltheWorkPrakeTheee (E. K. Heyer), (4) New Prayer (congregation standing silently), (5) MakeajoyfulNoice (W. T. Giffe), (6) Scripture Reading: Matthew 28:1-10, 1 Corinthians 15:35-49, (7) RejoiceintheLord (Tlnley Lyon), (8) (W. S. Martin), (9) Benediction and dismissal.

Foreign Businesses Close to Show Celebration

The so-called Easter is regarded as a great ceremony by the people of Europe and the United States. Therefore, foreign banks and companies have closed for three days, as usual, from Good Friday (April 7-9), the beginning of the Easter period (20th), and Easter Sunday (yesterday), to show their celebration. They will resume business today. As a result, the Bund-area trading exchange, which follows the foreign trading market, also took a three-day spring break during this time and reopened today.

Telegram Offices Busiest

During these three days, the minds of both old and new believers were particularly joyous. All relatives and friends in different places must celebrate with each other, either by letters or by telegrams. It is learned that telegram offices have been busier than usual in the past few days. It is estimated that the total number of telegrams sent and received each day is over 200 more than usual. The post office is also busier than usual.

Private Possession of Opium Pending Judgment 134

Cheng Bangshan from Anhui, at 1:40 PM the day before yesterday, was carrying a bamboo basket containing 19 small strips of opium, weighing 13 taels, when he passed Songpan Road. He was stopped by Chinese detective Wang Xichang and Chinese Constable No. 2790, who found his behavior suspicious. They stopped him, searched him, found the above-mentioned contraband, and also searched his home at No. 92, Lane 109, Zhoujiapai Road, seizing 20 small packets of opium and multiple sets of smoking paraphernalia. He was taken to the Yangshupu Police Station. The police chief ordered him to be detained. The next morning, he was escorted to the Criminal Division 3 of the Special Court. Attorney Li Zhishan of the Public Works Department described the previous circumstances. Then, the detectives reported the process of detaining the defendant and presented the evidence for inspection. Interrogated, Cheng confessed that the opium and other items belonged to a Zhang surnamed person who had fled. He claimed that Zhang asked him to keep them, but the judge, Wu Zehan, ordered him to be remanded in custody pending sentencing.

Fire in Xujiahui 135

At approximately 11 AM yesterday, a fire broke out in the home of Shen Songshi, a woman from Danyang, residing at No. 52, Lane 67, Ciyou Road, Xujiahui, West Shanghai. The fire, caused by carelessness while cooking, quickly spread through the roof. The police on duty quickly notified the fire department by telephone to dispatch a fire truck to the scene. The fire was soon extinguished. However, Shen Songshi suffered severe burns to her head, face, arms, and other areas. She has been admitted to the hospital for treatment.

Farmer's Wife Gives Birth to Twins, One Without a Head, One Without Limbs 136

Yin, the 25-year-old wife of Zhou Lian'gen, a farmer residing at Qujiaqiao, north of Meilongzhen, West Shanghai, had previously given birth to a son and a daughter, both of whom died prematurely. Recently, she became pregnant again and gave birth to twins the day before yesterday. (One child had no head, and one child had no limbs.) They both died shortly afterward. The Zhou family considered it inauspicious and immediately buried them.

Mudan Su Performs as Guest Star at Mingzhu Theater 141

She originally belonged to the Jinghua Ying Troupe, at the same time as Suzhou Mei and others. She has since gone to perform in the Americas, Annam and other places, which were deeply loved and appreciated by the overseas Chinese there. However, she lost her voice due to illness after only a few days on stage, so her talents were not fully displayed. By the time her voice recovered, Hua Shanyu's contract had expired. She originally planned to return to Guangdong and make a short stay in Hangzhou, but she has now accepted the invitation of the Mingzhu Theater on Laobazhi Road and will perform as a guest star for two nights, Monday and Tuesday. The plays are the famous Cantonese operas "Night Hanging White Hibiscus" and "Wu Song," a rare opportunity for Cantonese opera lovers in Shanghai.

Establishment of the Cargo Warehouse Workers' Union 145

There are numerous cargo warehouses in Shanghai, providing services to tens of thousands of workers. However, they have always lacked organization, like scattered sand. As a result, not only does the relationship between labor and management often become estranged, but the workers themselves also lack protection. Lu Dazhou, a cargo warehouse worker at Taikoo Steampship Company, and others have initiated the organization of the Shanghai Cargo Warehouse Workers' Trade Union. The application has been approved and filed by the Party and government authorities. The inaugural general meeting of representatives was held yesterday at the union's premises at No. 1, Huining Lane, Fuyou Road. Representatives from the Party, government, and the General Labor Union attended to supervise. Lu Dazhou, Liao Zengxun, and other eleven people were elected as directors and supervisors. It is heard that after the establishment of the union, it will expand its publicity so that all cargo warehouse workers can participate.

Record of the Re-election of the 37th District Branch of the Citizens' Association 146

The 37th District Branch of the First Special District Citizens' Association of this city held its second re-election meeting yesterday at 3:00 PM in the assembly hall of its office at No. 9, Lane 20, North Fook Road. Huanqiu Enamel Factory Expands Business. The Huanqiu Enamel Factory outlet at 510 Tianjin Road, Shanghai (behind the Sincere Company), has been established for five years. Gao Changxing Aged Shaoxing Wine Arrives in Shanghai. The Gao Weixing Wine Shop on Fourth Road in Shanghai is famous for its richly fragrant wines. Its various Shaoxing wines are of exceptional color, fragrance, and taste, earning it a reputation throughout Shanghai. Its business is thriving, making it the leader in Shanghai's wine industry. It is reported that the shop has recently received a large shipment of aged wine from the Shaoxing factory, all brewed between 1913 and 1914 and stored for over twenty years. It is now being sold as usual. Its pure aroma and potent strength are unmatched by other brands.

Dahu Bank Launches Small Savings Program. It is simple, convenient, and innovative, truly a unique addition to the savings regulations.

Chunqiu

Snippets 151

— (Jin Xiong Yu)

Elsewhere, "people" are "people," but in Shanghai, "people" have become "money." Look: in the morning, rickshaw pullers with smiling faces take "people" as "fare" and pull them away. In bookstores, stores with big discounts play music, treating "people" as "the price of goods," welcoming customers. At night, landlords are so eager, treating "people" as "rent," opening the door to let them in.

Farmers in the fields, "heave-ho, heave-ho..." together carry the crops back home. When I see that, I only feel admiration. Western-style couples in department stores, "murmuring and mumbling," walk arm in arm up and down. When I see that, I only feel disgusted.

Ah! I thought I was sleeping in my beloved's arms, my chest pressed tightly against hers, but when I opened my eyes, I was still lonely, embracing the quilt alone. In that instant, I felt the pain of lost love.

Spring Scenery of West Lake in the Late Song Dynasty 152

— 19

In the spring, countless people depend on West Lake for their livelihood; therefore, Hangzhou people have the saying "three winters rely on one spring." West Lake is at its best in spring, not only now, but it has always been so. Qu Zongji of the Ming Dynasty wrote "West Lake's Four Seasons, Looking South," which describes the spring scenery of West Lake at that time: "West Lake scenery, spring days are best when sunny. Beneath the flowers, music and songs at the young masters' banquets, along the water's edge, beautiful people walk, ten miles of singing." How prosperous it already was! However, the spring scenery of West Lake in the late Song Dynasty was even more prosperous than in the Ming Dynasty. Here, I extract a section from the "West Lake Fu" by Bai Tingyu of the Yuan Dynasty to give a glimpse:

"Especially the dragon boats in pairs, drums pounding, display hundreds of performances on the water, erecting six markers in the heart of the lake... The viewers' boats are in two rows, like broad paths; the welcomers' silk banners are like long forests. Every five steps, there is a pavilion, serving wine, tea, and pastries. The sounds of music and singing boil, carriages bustle. Willow branches touch the ground, flower formations line the clouds. Shuttle doors and swings appear and disappear in the emerald greenery; dancing costumes and singing fans twirl in the fragrant dust... Eyes cannot take it all in, steps cannot follow. Imagining the Song Sister Geng of Huai and Lu, still presenting crane dances performed by actors. Cutting silk and arranging flowers on plates, molding sugar into scales to thread on willow branches. Decorating wooden soldiers on small crossbars, stringing furniture on long bamboo. Oars and arrows stir up thunder in the air, kites compete with the warp and weft of the nine heavens. Catapults, ivory crossbows, painting sticks and splashing basins. (Note: "Treading on mixed talent" and "splashing minister basin" are both water games.) Silk socks step on the waves, golden hairpins illuminate the spring. Often there are sons who gather red and pick green, and how can there be no guests who seek secluded beauty? This is just a mention of a fraction of the ninety days of spring."

It is said that Tingyu was born during the Lizong era. What he describes above is a depiction of the spring scenery of West Lake in the late Song Dynasty, the liveliness of which is no less than that of Yu Xin's "Spring Fu." However, at that time, the country was already in a precarious state, yet the people still embellished peace and lived in a drunken dream. How can we not sigh deeply after reading this!

Young Master Kite 153

— Yan

From the kite-flying competition in the capital's Yuhuatai, where 150,000 people watched, I thought of the Young Master Kite of Changshu twenty years ago. All kites are named after what they resemble in shape, such as eagle kites, butterfly kites, centipede kites, etc. Only this Young Master Kite is named after the person who flies it. Therefore, the Young Master Kite is the kite played by young masters and sons.

The Young Master Kite does not compete in size, but rather emphasizes its smallness and exquisiteness. It is made of finely woven and smooth bamboo strips for the kite's frame, covered with cicada-wing gauze that can be stretched or shrunk. When stretched, it is colorful and beautiful, and when shrunk, it folds like a fan and is placed in a bag. The bag is also exquisitely made, using brocade and silk, embroidered with flowers, birds, insects, and fish, and adorned with tassels, mostly made by young women of noble families. The kite is placed in the brocade bag, and the bag is hung at the waist, just like the elegant scholars of old hanging their fans from their waistbands. The kite's string is also made of white silk instead of coarse hemp. The colorful kite, paired with the pure white string, enhances its beauty.

In the bright spring, with gentle spring breezes, young masters and sons would agree to go to the suburbs to fly kites as a game. Behind each young master, there would always be a servant to assist in unraveling the silk thread and releasing the kite. They would either guide it themselves or hand it over to the servant, while they admired it from the side. The colorful kites stood steadily in the wind in the sky, light and carefree. The colorful young masters walked slowly back and forth on the ground, speaking softly and laughing gently. The spring scenery was enchanting, the kites were enchanting, and the young masters were enchanting. This enchanting scene was so delightful! When they were tired, they would order the servant to help wind the thread and retrieve the kite, then place it back in the brocade bag, tie it to their waists, and slowly return home along the setting sun and evening breeze.

In recent years, things have been depressed everywhere, and the bourgeoisie has also declined. The qualifications of young masters and sons no longer exist, so these elegant pastimes of twenty years ago are no longer seen today. This simple pleasure of flying kites also evokes a sense of滄桑 in this era. It is regrettable!

After the Stresa Conference, the United Kingdom, France, and Italy Tried to Support a Collapsing Building

Little Western Paradise 154

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 12: Ashamed of Being Naked, She Avoids Guests Behind a Curtain; Diligently Saving Kerosene, He Copies Books at Dawn

When Bei Hai heard that Yue Ying was here, he himself felt a little hot in the face. He thought to himself, what is the reason for this? Mr. Cheng let her sleep in his bed, but he hid away. If a respectable male friend came, wouldn't there be a misunderstanding? Regardless of any suspicion, I have to sit in this room and study. If someone comes, I can also explain things for Mr. Cheng. Thinking this, he walked back into the room, ignoring the person on the bed, and sat down at the table near the window as if he owned the place, spreading out the books he had brought. Yue Ying inside the mosquito net could see clearly. She knew that Wang Bei Hai was a very proper person and would not do anything untoward, but still, being stark naked and sleeping in someone else's bed was a very embarrassing thing. Her heart was uneasy, and she just kept tossing and turning in bed. Bei Hai couldn't bear it any longer, so he spoke to her inside the net: "Is that Miss Zhu inside? Are you feeling unwell?" Yue Ying was too embarrassed to answer and continued to lie there silently. Bei Hai saw a thermos on the table and picked it up. The bottle was very heavy, so it must be filled with water. So, he said, "Miss Zhu, there is hot water here. Shall I pour you a cup to drink?" Yue Ying saw that the man was being so attentive that she felt too embarrassed to continue ignoring him, so she replied, "I dare not trouble you." Bei Hai then moved a square stool and placed it in front of the bed. He poured a large cup of hot water, added some tea concentrate from the teapot, and carefully placed it on the stool. Then, he smiled at the net and said, "Take it and drink it yourself." (187)

Imperial Fragrance Faintly Recorded 155

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

They also have a characteristic, which is that they are rich in the spirit of "artisan work," meaning working only for the sake of "art" and "work." Each pair of phoenix shoes takes at least a month to make, and within that month, the amount of effort they put into each pair of phoenix shoes is immeasurable. However, the result of their efforts can only be seen by the Empress Dowager herself, and even if the Empress Dowager likes them and uses them, only a few of us have the opportunity to admire them. Who else can discover their ingenious craftsmanship? Therefore, when they are making them, they never intend to boast to the public, but only want to make this craft as perfect as their ideals! Moreover, most of the embroidered shoes they make are relegated to the cold palace by the Empress Dowager, and are always guarded by two old eunuchs who are full and have nothing to do. They have no chance to see the world, and they are equal to working hard for nothing. But they are not discouraged and still work with all their effort. How can this kind of spirit be possessed by ordinary artists and master craftsmen?

Since these young girls live such extraordinary lives in such a special environment, their thoughts inevitably become very unique. It seems that they are very indifferent to getting married and raising children. I have also indirectly heard their comments, and they are generally satisfied with the status quo. They regard those squares of tribute satin as their husbands, and those skeins of silk thread as their children. In their hearts, they truly love these two companions who are always with them. (297)

Foreigners and Dogs 156

— Yiyiguan Master

In Shanghai, which is praised as the "Paris of the East," whether on the roads of the British Concession or the French Concession, one often sees "foreigners," especially "foreign women," walking around. Eight or nine out of ten are leading a dog, or two, or even three. Big and small, of all kinds, wagging their tails, following their owners, or leading their owners.

Sometimes, a "motorcar" whirs past. Inside, in addition to the "foreigner" sitting there, there is often a dog squatting on it. Head held high, tongue lolling, proudly looking at everything! As a result, its owner seems even more impressive.

I don't know why, but these things invariably make me think of the parks in the concessions. Before they were opened, "Chinese and dogs" were "not allowed to enter." At the time, we Chinese felt that this was an insult! However, now seeing "foreigners" and dogs so "inseparable," it suddenly dawns on me! I feel that the word "dog" in the phrase "Chinese and dogs not allowed to enter" really referred to the dogs kept by the Chinese! As for "foreign dogs," of course, they were not included. Otherwise, if "foreign dogs" were also restricted from entering and leaving the park, would their owners be willing?

Alas! In this light, that notice saying "Chinese and dogs not allowed to enter" was tantamount to announcing to the Chinese people: "Only foreigners and foreign dogs are allowed to enter!" Thinking about it carefully, we are all the same, so what is insulting about it? Hehe!

One Calyx Red 157

— (Hong Jingshan)

Returned from the sea to lie ill in Baisha Village in the winter month of Jiaxu, taking stock of the factory gates. Adding Sighs, both are written with a stone broom.

Shadowed by the small building's gloom, the cold ripples reflect my image, graying hair too heavy for the hairpin. Returning, ah, returning, the year draws to a close, myriad feelings given over to oblivion. Beyond the frozen mist, the pruned branches rustle in the evening, just as weary birds fly three or two to return to their nests. Likewise drifting, several times ceasing the construction, such a descent. Looking back on the Jiangguan journey, tears still stain my collar, no heart to pluck the sword. The streams and mountains of my hometown, childhood fishing and frolicking, like a dream, afraid to seek them out again. Completely inviting mountain apes and cranes, yet in the vast expanse, who will send money to buy a mountain? Waiting to dispel sorrow with clear wine, but sorrow is too deep!

World News

Random Tidbits from the Yokohama Exposition (Part 1) 158

— Ji Yun

Yokohama suffered the most severe damage during the Great Kanto Earthquake in Japan, with almost the entire city being reduced to rubble. After more than ten years of arduous effort, its surface facilities have already surpassed pre-disaster levels. The exposition commemorates this recovery movement, and thus it serves as a display of local products from various regions. The Yokohama Municipal Government initiated the event, with various prefectures joining in. Territories such as Korea, Taiwan, and areas under South Seas governance also have exhibits. Additionally, there are Manchurian and Siamese pavilions. These areas neither suffered from the earthquake nor underwent reconstruction, making their inclusion quite inappropriate and incongruous.

The Opening of the Port Memorial Hall showcases Yokohama's female-oriented progress, with the construction of telephone systems, automobiles, and running water all represented through illustrations and models. At the entrance stand two Japanese individuals dressed in the attire of police officers from the port's opening era. They wear conical straw hats and short brown jackets, with a white "Sun" character emblazoned on the back of their necks, the meaning of which remains unclear. A Japanese sword is tucked at their waists. To the side, there are also old-fashioned sword and spear racks, holding various long-handled weapons.

The Reconstruction Hall features numerous photographs depicting the harrowing scenes of the disaster, evoking the extreme fear experienced during the earthquake. A map, spanning over ten feet, is compiled from aerial photography, ensuring its detail and accuracy. Tall Western-style buildings appear as mere grains, with magnifying glasses provided to aid viewers with less acute vision.

Although there is a large character at the top of this exposition, it is actually quite small. Besides the entirety of Yokohama's Yamashita Park, there is another area across the road, which is even smaller. The middle section is further divided into two parts by a road, so they built wooden bridges to accommodate the crowds, a rather crude method. Due to the difficulty of transporting large-scale machinery, few such items are on display. The exhibits in the various pavilions mainly consist of light industrial metal products, lacquerware, carpentry, textiles, and daily necessities.

Japanese women also use very small folding fans, with a ladder-style construction similar to those in our country. They have large white ribs and small wooden ribs, with the fan surface being only three or four inches wide, narrower than the ribs on the back. Both the fan surface and ribs are printed with various patterns of flowers and plants, with elegant and subtle colors, which is quite novel. The greatest characteristic of Japanese manufactured goods is their ability to utilize waste materials. Bamboo scraps and large wood shavings are all used as materials. A beautiful seashell, with a small figure attached, becomes an ornament. This is similar to the people in Jiangbei, China, who place powdered figures in clam shells. Nara has sacred deer that live in groups in the forests, and the Japanese do not dare to harm them. The local people use the shed antlers to make cigarette holders and ornaments.

Japanese matches are mostly in flat boxes, with each box only holding about thirty matches, sold for one foreign cent. Large stores often paste advertisements on them and give them to customers, with each person receiving four or five boxes. Therefore, in Japan, if you smoke, you almost don't need to buy matches. The advertisements on the boxes are gold, silver, and colored, small and exquisitely designed. Printing costs in Japan are very cheap.

Sports News

International Football Federation Decides on World Games Football Regulations 159

(Havas Agency, Paris, 20th) The Executive Committee of the International Football Federation, meeting here, has decided on the football regulations for next year's Olympic Games: (1) The length of the field shall be at least 100 yards and shall not exceed 130 yards; (2) The width of the field shall be at least 50 yards and shall not exceed 100 yards; (3) The radius of the center circle for the kick-off point shall be 10 feet; (4) The goal crossbar shall be 8 feet long and the upright posts 8 feet high; (5) The ball circumference shall be at least 17 inches and shall not exceed 28 inches. In addition, the Executive Committee has also decided on the field regulations for future international football matches: (1) The length shall be between 110 yards and 120 yards; (2) The width shall be between 70 yards and 80 yards; (3) The weight of the ball at the start of the match shall be between 369 grams and 425 grams. The above regulations will be implemented at the start of the next football season.

Western League Soccer A Group Concludes, Donghua Defeats Ennis, Result 2-1 165

In this year's Western League soccer tournament, except for the final match between Xingguang and St. Francis in Group E, the other matches such as the Scott Cup, Group A Cup, Zilin Cup, Junior Cup, and Group B, C, and D Cups, have all concluded successively. Yesterday afternoon, Donghua met Ennis at Shenyuan, in the last match of Group A. Both sides were evenly matched, and the situation was extremely balanced. Donghua finally relied on the bravery of its entire team to win 2-1. It is not easy for a Group B team to play so vibrantly.

First Half

The match began with alternating attacks and defenses, and the teams were evenly matched. After about ten minutes, Donghua's Zhou Guangzhong got the ball and advanced. The enemy defense resulted in a corner kick. Yang Renwei kicked it well, and Qian Zuozhi hooked it into the net from the crowd. After the goal, the British army counterattacked strongly. Once, Chen Gongyu illegally hit someone in the penalty area and was penalized with a penalty kick. The enemy center forward kicked it, and it went to the left. Then, they kicked a free kick outside the twelve-yard line, and it went to the right. One left and one right, complementing each other interestingly. In the first half, Donghua took the lead with one goal.

Second Half

Changing sides, Ennis tried to cheer up and came fiercely, but because Donghua's defense was strict, there was no chance to take advantage of. Ten minutes before the end of the game, Ennis launched a surprise attack. The right winger got a chance to take a corner kick. Guan Dangan slapped it not far, and Tai Hede sent it into the net corner, making it 1-1. The situation suddenly became tense. Feng Nianhan entered the abdomen alone, and after aiming, he swept it away. Goalkeeper Smithon jumped up to catch it, and Qian Zuozhi slammed on it. Smithon slipped the ball he had in his grasp. Before the central kick-off, the battle ended. Donghua won 2-1.

Surrounded by Green Mountains and Wildflowers Like Hairpins, the Third Shandong Provincial National Arts Examination Opens, Male and Female Heroes Offer Themselves 166

Jinan Correspondence: The third Shandong Provincial National Arts Examination, after several months of preparation, opened this morning (20th) at the Provincial People's Sports Field at the foot of Thousand Buddha Mountain. The morning sun was slightly bright, the mountains were verdant, and the wildflowers were like brocade. The officials of the conference and the male and female examinees arrived at the venue very early. People from all walks of life took time out to watch, which was extremely lively. The heads of various agencies and guests included Governor of Shandong Province Han Fuju, Qingdao Mayor Shen Honglie, Jiaoji Railway Committee Chairman Ge Guangting, Director of the Education Department He Siyuan, Provincial Committee Member Lin Jiqing, Provincial Executive Committee Member Li Wenqi, and dozens of consultants and senators from the Provincial Government. At 7:00 am, a meeting was held in front of the main building. The military band was in the south, the first row in front of the stage was for the conference officials, and behind them were all 610 examinees, with orderly discipline. After the meeting started according to the ritual, the Chairman of the Examination Committee, Han Fuqu, gave the opening speech, followed by honorary Examination Committee Chairman Shen Honglie, Guidance Committee Chairman Ge Guangting, Yang Songshan, the supervising committee member sent by the Central National Arts Hall, and judge Liu Buxian, who delivered training speeches successively. Afterwards, Ma Liang and Zhang Ming delivered speeches on behalf of the guests. The photography ceremony was completed at 8:30 am. The performance began at 9:00 am. The ones who took the stage in order were the vine shield and broadsword team of the Nanguan National Arts Society of this city, the entire team of Qingdao athletes, and the performance troupe of children from the National Arts Hall. Among them, the female athletes Yue Xiuyun and Jiang Ailan from the Qingdao team attracted the most attention. The performance ended at 11:00 am, and there was a break. The competition started at 1:00 pm. At that time, there were about 10,000 spectators, and the number of people was unprecedented.

Performing Vine Shield Tactics: The first Shandong Provincial Examination only involved unarmed combat, wrestling, long weapons, and short weapons. The second examination added archery and slingshot performances. This examination also added vine shield tactics, and the atmosphere of reviving the past is becoming increasingly strong. According to legend, the vine shield was a weapon used in the era of knife and spear warfare in ancient China. It has been abandoned and has not been seen in the world for more than 40 years, becoming a historical relic. The National Arts Society on Desheng South Street in this city has recently been practicing this kind of tactics. Today, the president Jiang Laibin led the vine shield team to perform on the field. There are about 40 team members, with green turbans wrapped around their heads, the ends of the turbans hanging behind their heads, and wearing green uniforms. The left hand holds a round shield woven from thin bamboo, covered with a yellow cloth, painted with a tiger head shape, and the right hand holds a single sword. At first glance, it looks like a martial arts performance on the stage. Under the command of vine shield teachers Yang Derun and Yang Jingyi, National Arts teacher Li Kuixiang, and archery teacher Zhang Kehan, the team first performed group exercises, moving forward and backward in accordance with the law, and also performed somersaults with shields, shouting and shaking the earth. Afterwards, they performed duels, broadswords against shields, spears against vine shields, etc. Finally, they stacked vine shields into a mountain, with people behind it, and then performed double duels, climbing the mountain and flipping somersaults down. The surrounding spectators cheered, and gray-haired old men nodded in praise, sighing that they had not seen it for decades. According to the president, this kind of skill can be divided into broadsword shield, double sword shield, Ma Yi shield, Shaozi shield, spear shield, meteor shield, and various formations. Now, because they have not practiced for a long time, they feel quite unfamiliar.
