The Cunwen Association Was Formally Established Yesterday; Jiang Kanghu Reported on the Attitude of the Cunwen Association; Seven Directors Elected and a Declaration Issued 176

The Cunwen Association, organized by academic circles in this city, held its inaugural meeting at the Municipal Public Education Center at 10 a.m. yesterday, to discuss the charter, declaration, and election of officers, and to pass proposals. The meeting proceeded as follows:

Members Present

Jiang Kanghu, Pan Gongzhan, Yao Minghui, Wang Xishen, Hu Puan, Jiang Jianbai, Ma Gongyu, Mao Xiaocen, Zhu Xiangwan, Qian Huafo, Lü Hailan, Ding Shoutang, Yuan Zenghuang, Guo Butao, Gao Chuiwan, Chen Gongsu, Shao Mingjiu, Chen Cuina, Zhang Feng, Chen Zhuzun, and over two hundred others attended. Mao Yun, representing the Municipal Party Department, and Nie Haifan, representing the Municipal Education Bureau, attended to provide guidance. The presidium consisted of Jiang Kanghu, Pan Gongzhan, Yao Minghui, Ma Gongyu, Wang Xishen, Chen Zhuzun, Hu Puan, and seven others.

Chairman's Report

After performing the customary rituals, Chairman Jiang Kanghu reported, saying in brief: "The weather is very good today, and holding the Cunwen Association meeting within the literary circle, the time and place are both favorable. There are supporters and opponents of the founding of the Cunwen Association. Let us leave aside the supporters. The opponents are, of course, unaware of the association's purpose. The misunderstanding lies not in the name 'Cunwen' (Preserve Literature), but in specific issues. (1) The problem of vernacular writing: some people think that the Cunwen Association opposes vernacular writing. In fact, I promoted vernacular writing more than thirty years ago. It makes no sense to oppose vernacular writing. However, I believe that articles have different styles, and writing should be free. Each should do what they are suited to do without restrictions. The function of vernacular writing is primarily for enlightenment and secondarily for making things accessible. But apart from these two points, we still advocate using classical Chinese in textbooks above the middle school level. (2) The problem of phonetic script: the Cunwen Association also promotes phonetic script and phonetic symbols. However, if someone were to exclusively use symbols and abandon Chinese characters, the Cunwen Association would absolutely oppose it. (3) The problem of shorthand characters or simplified characters: the Cunwen Association also approves of shorthand characters to a considerable extent and does not oppose them. This is our attitude. For the progress of future work, we hope that at least Chinese teachers above the middle school level will engage in this Cunwen movement. We also hope that students above the general middle school level will have a basic knowledge of classical Chinese, and even if they cannot write articles in classical Chinese, they should at least understand and be able to read classical Chinese." The representatives of the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Education Bureau also delivered speeches, as did Yao Minghui and others.

Discussion of Proposals

Next, the proposals were discussed: (1) The draft charter of the Cunwen Association was read and amended item by item by the chairman and passed. (2) The draft declaration of the Cunwen Association was resolved to be revised and published by Champion. (3) A proposal to petition the Ministry of Education in the name of the conference to issue an order to all primary schools nationwide to add two hours per week of simple classical Chinese reading from the middle grades onwards was resolved and passed.

Election of Officers

Finally, officers were elected. Under the supervision of Mao Yun, representing the Municipal Party Department, and Nie Haifan, representing the Municipal Education Bureau, Jiang Kanghu, Wang Xishen, Pan Gongzhan, Yao Minghui, Hu Puan, Ma Gongyu, and Qian Jibo were elected as directors. Mao Xiaocen, Jiang Jianbai, and Zhang Feng were elected as alternate directors. The meeting was adjourned for a photograph at noon.

Conference Declaration

The declaration of the Cunwen Association stated: "Since the Cunwen movement was launched, voices of support and opposition have arisen everywhere. Let us leave aside the supporters for now and focus on the arguments of the opponents. A says, 'Literature has not been abandoned; why preserve it? This is baseless moaning and shooting at random.' This person has not considered Yan's four preservations. Human nature, learning, and governance have never been completely absent from this land, yet Yan alone held the warning of 'its loss, its loss.' Is it not because taking care will preserve it, and identifying it early is essential? B says, 'Classical Chinese is dead, like a corpse. It should be buried without decoration.' This contradicts A's statement. Believing this, it is our responsibility to revive the flesh and bones. Once the sword is drawn, there is no turning back, because preserving literature preserves everything, and abandoning literature abandons everything. Literature may not encompass all of culture, but culture cannot be separated from literature.' C says, 'No, what should be abandoned now is only classical Chinese. The rise of vernacular language marks the advancement of culture.' But advancement must be based on what is already there and added to it. How can we rely on decades of creation to erase millennia of heritage? D says, 'No, classical Chinese should only be listed as a special subject for archaeologists to study and artists to appreciate. Why should the public and students study it?' If so, history and culture will be forever separated from the nation, and the nation's vitality will almost be extinguished.' E says, 'Studying it is fine, but only to understand it, not to be arrogant. Reciting classical Chinese or learning vernacular should not be required. However, if you only read but don't write, the meaning will not be precise, and the application will not be broad, and it will become like Latin in European and American schools, transforming from a living language into a dead one. But Latin can die, while classical Chinese cannot. If classical Chinese dies, then language will differ by region, and writing will also differ by region, making it impossible to unify the national language and leading to the division of the national script. Language changes with the times, and writing also changes with the times. Every four or five hundred years, it must be translated once. What are the gains and losses of this?' F says, 'What's the harm? Vernacular writing and phonetic transcription are innovative literature. The elimination of classical Chinese writing and characters is appropriate. Why not learn from Japan's past? Chinese characters were originally imported, and kana has long been in common use. Phonetic transcription is most convenient, so why mix the two? Yet classical Chinese writing and characters have ultimately not been abandoned. What is the reason? It is worth pondering, especially since it is our own heritage.' G says, 'Not abandoning Chinese characters and classical Chinese is fine, but textbooks are readily available in bookstores. Why read the classics, histories, philosophers, and collections? Why make them the standard for literature? Alas, errors are passed down, and bad habits become the norm. Abandoning the original and demolishing the center, what is left? Moreover, literary standards should be based on current practice, as all countries do. Now, we abandon the Zhou tripod and fill it with Kang earthenware, discarding the essence and feeding on dross. What could be worse?' H says, 'The classics, histories, philosophers, and collections are also dross. Quoting erroneous and absurd words from the Four Divisions to attack each other leads to the belief that everything can be demolished. Finding fault with everything and stopping eating because of one choking is like letting yourself freeze and starve. Who can you blame?' I says, 'The evolution of writing is roughly the same as language. The Zhou, Qin, Han, and Tang dynasties did not follow each other. Engaging in stagnation and staying in the past is useless.' This idea seems right, but the change in writing should be very slow, and we should let it evolve naturally. If we change everything into vernacular, it will create a clear divide, which is inconvenient. J says, 'There are many excellent works by vernacular writers. Leaving aside contemporary ones, works like Romance of the Three Kingdoms, Water Margin, Scholars, and Dream of the Red Chamber are in no way inferior to classical Chinese.' This argument is also valid, but up to now, all vernacular writers have been skilled in classical Chinese. A lion fighting a ghost is doubly energetic. If they did not know classical Chinese, would they have achieved these results?' Summarizing the above ten arguments, the answers have been detailed. Other derogatory remarks are intentionally left unsaid, out of respect for individuals and to avoid counterattacks. In short, we acknowledge the value of vernacular language but should not abandon classical Chinese because of it. Phonetic transcription has its functions but should not replace Chinese characters. Vernacular writing can be written but should not prohibit people from promoting classical Chinese. There are many good articles in vernacular, but it should not be regarded as orthodox literature. As the association is now being established, we have presented these scattered opinions, both positive and negative, in a comprehensive declaration."

Li Jinxi Makes Another Statement: The Advantages and Disadvantages of Phonetically Annotated Chinese Characters; Responding to Chen Heqin's Doubts 177

(Beiping Express) Recently, Chen Heqin, Director of the Chinese Education Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, "Again Discussed the Advantages and Disadvantages of Phonetic Chinese Characters." He responded to the remarks of Li Jinxi, a standing member of the National Language Unification Association. Now, Li has made another statement as follows:

Auxiliary Tools

(1) Mr. Chen says that the phonetic symbols and punctuation marks differ in complexity. But there are sixteen types of completely new punctuation marks, which are not as simple as a dot, a dash, or a line. Only thirty-seven phonetic symbols are used in the national language, which is not comparable to the numerous and complex strokes of Chinese characters. Punctuation marks should be integrated with the meaning of Chinese characters, and phonetic symbols should be integrated with the pronunciation of Chinese characters. Their uses are equivalent, and their shapes must not be confused with Chinese characters. Readers can save time and increase understanding with these two auxiliary tools, without a doubt.

Facts Do Not Match

(2) Mr. Chen's investigation of the situation in Japanese newspapers seems to be inconsistent with the facts. Ordinary Japanese newspapers and popular magazines, except for the number of Chinese characters like one, two, three, etc., which are not annotated, all Chinese characters are annotated. Mr. Chen's so-called "only one or two out of ten" probably refers to high-level literary works, where only rare Chinese characters are occasionally annotated with kana. (According to my own observation, recent Japanese literary works, even more popular ones, are fully annotated with kana.) As for printed materials in six-point type, children should not read them in the first place. If children's books also use six-point type, even without annotation, I know that Mr. Chen cannot guarantee that they will not become nearsighted.

Avoid Harm

(3) In the teaching process, the training of readers should focus attention on Chinese characters, not the annotations. Where does the "disturbance" come from with unknown characters? If there are no annotations, it is a fact that Chinese characters are misrecognized and misheard. How can annotation lead to errors? If there are annotations, unknown characters can be understood by looking at the side, which can at least save the trouble of looking up dictionaries and asking around. How can annotation lead to time consumption? The various harms mentioned by Mr. Chen arise from the lack of annotation next to Chinese characters. Only by promoting phonetically annotated Chinese characters can these harms be avoided.

Overshadowing the Main Thing

(4) All problems should be studied experimentally, but the tools and conditions for research must be complete. Several years ago, a friend feared that phonetic annotation of Chinese characters would overshadow the main thing in the future, and children would only recognize the annotations and neglect the Chinese characters. Therefore, he conducted experiments in a civilian primary school in Dongcheng here. After a year, the students in this class recognized more Chinese characters. He was satisfied and supported phonetic symbols. But I think this kind of experiment is unreliable because the materials used were only a mimeographed phonetic textbook and a daily phonetic newspaper. Whether phonetic symbols will overshadow the main thing in the future is not considered by me, but it is premature for a friend to decide based on this. Therefore, it is necessary to prepare phonetically annotated Chinese character molds and print a large number of reading materials before conducting various studies. Otherwise, it will be detrimental to the authenticity of academic experts' research.

Main Purpose

(5) Mr. Chen has now seen the effectiveness of national language education for overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. It should be known that national language teachers in overseas Chinese schools have been using phonetic symbols as a tool for teaching the national language in recent years. This is a fact that everyone has seen and heard. What is lacking now is this kind of textbook with phonetic symbols and characters side by side, as well as general phonetic reading materials. According to the report of the National Language Association's special commissioner in Southeast Asia, if there are such publications, the effectiveness of national language education and literacy will be greatly expanded. Special commissioners in Mongolia and Xinjiang have particularly fervent proposals for this. The motivation for the government to allocate funds to cast copper molds for phonetically annotated Chinese characters this time is half for education in the border areas and overseas Chinese education. Mr. Chen's so-called "unifying the national language and unifying the national pronunciation" is indeed one of its goals, but the main purpose is to assist literacy and increase the efficiency of national education. This point should not be ignored. The National Language Association once proposed that the time for public education is currently very limited, while the inculcation of national consciousness and various common senses is also urgent. This kind of tool to assist literacy should be studied by following the example of Japan to maintain a permanent connection. Once the symbols are mastered, the meaning will be clear, and hearing will lead to understanding, making things twice as easy with half the effort. Why should we be concerned about "redundancy"?

Reading Movement Day 13: Wang Xinming Lectures on Literary Research 178

Yesterday was the thirteenth day of the National Reading Movement Conference, sponsored by the Chinese Culture Construction Association. The association specially invited Wang Xinming to lecture on "How to Study Literature." The full text of the lecture is recorded as follows:

Today, at the Reading Movement Conference sponsored by the Chinese Culture Association, I am asked to talk about the problem of "how to study literature." I will now offer my personal opinions for your reference.

In general, literature differs from natural sciences and social sciences. Natural science is the study of explaining phenomena in the natural world. Social science is the tool for explaining various social systems and criticizing various social problems. Literature, however, is the tool for describing nature and society. Natural science and social science emphasize reason and reality, while literature emphasizes emotion and ideals. In fact, this is only a rough distinction. If we examine it more closely, we will know that literature, which describes nature and society, also carries the task of explaining natural phenomena, explaining various social systems, and criticizing various social problems. However, there is an insurmountable watershed between natural science, social science, and literature in the pure theoretical research and the complete expression of emotion.

We believe that there is a common point between literature and natural science and social science. This common point is that all take enriching human life as a prerequisite.

Generally, people regard literature as knowledge without practical application, thinking that literature is a kind of impractical luxury. It is not too much to have it, and not too little to not have it. In fact, literature is a very valuable thing. It not only has the great power of subtly influencing society and deeply affecting people's hearts, but it can also trigger earth-shattering trends. For example, Plato's Republic, Rousseau's theory of natural human rights, the American Declaration of Independence, the French Marseillaise, and Marx's Communist Manifesto were all just novels, articles, or songs at the time, but later they all became the driving force behind political and social revolutions. This is enough to illustrate the greatness of literary influence.

As for the method of studying literature, it varies with the purpose of studying literature. What I hope everyone will study now is the relationship between literature and its background. We should know that the literature of each country and each era must be attached to its special color, either a color that encourages conquering other countries and tribes, or a color that inspires resistance to other countries and tribes, thus forming a "national literature." Regarding this point, we can get considerable proof in literary history.

For example, in China during the Ming and Qing dynasties, wasn't the literature most popular in the lower classes novels and dramas with the theme of conquering other countries and tribes? There are too many names for these novels and dramas to list them all. In a word, they are always "Conquering the West," "Conquering the East," "Pacifying the South," and "Sweeping the North." They all say that a small country around China suddenly changed its always-submissive attitude, mobilized troops to invade China. At first, China was unprepared, and the troops seemed to have entered an uninhabited land everywhere. Later, the emperor became furious and ordered generals to go on expeditions. A large army marched mightily to a certain country. Although at first, because the generals were cowardly and unwise, they fell into the enemy's trap and suffered several defeats, later someone ran out of the army with a height of eight or nine feet and superhuman strength, volunteered, and the enemy general became a ghost under his knife. Therefore, the emperor issued an edict to withdraw the troops and rewarded the courtiers. The emergence of this kind of literature is by no means accidental. The background is the rampant desire to conquer among the general public at that time. In addition, there is also a kind of literature aimed at eliminating traitors because the national consciousness of the literati at that time was unclear, and some people had the fear of "Yi becoming China." Therefore, they wrote many novels and dramas against traitors. Yue Zhuan can be the representative of this kind of literature. Qin Hui, shaped in Yue Zhuan, is the standard traitor they opposed.

This is just one example. In fact, this kind of example is too numerous to mention. For example, before Poland regained its independence, its literature was all about promoting national self-help. The literature at the time when Korea had just been destroyed was all about the ideal of restoring the Three Hans. The literature after the Russian October Revolution was all about carrying the slogan of "Capitalism attacking Soviet Russia." They all sufficiently prove that literature and its background are inseparable. What kind of background there is, what kind of literature should be produced.

Looking at the development of literature from a purely social point of view, it is also different in each country according to its social ideology. For example, why do Dickens's novels and Shakespeare's dramas mostly depict the dark side of society? There is no other reason. It is because the society in England at that time was so dark that they wanted to arouse the awareness of the general public to transform society. Therefore, he could not but work hard to criticize the dark society.

In short, the most important thing in studying literature is to understand the background of the literature. If you can understand its background, then you can know its central consciousness, and your own path forward will not be blocked by "preconceived ideas."

Pan Gongzhan Convenes a Reading Guidance Symposium; Forty or Fifty Scholars Arrived and the Guidance Methods Were Very Detailed 179

Yesterday (the 21st) was the thirteenth day of the National Reading Movement. Mr. Pan Gongzhan, the president of Chenbao (Morning Post), specially invited scholars and celebrities from this city to the Shanghai United Club for the supplementary publication of the newspaper "Chenyi" (Morning Ant) to hold a "Reading Guidance Symposium." Those who arrived included Huang Zao Xiong, Li Shaozhe, Wu Zifu, Hu Huaichen, Shen Pengfei, Zhu Yingpeng, Wang Xinming, Chen Zehua, Tai Shuangqiu, Tao Youchuan, Zhang Ziping, He Bingsong, Sun Hanbing, Chen Gaochu, Liu Baimin, Fan Zhongyun, Tong Xingbai, Zhao Jingshen, Ye Qing, Cao Juren, Wang Fuquan, Pan Yangyao, and more than fifty others. All of them were highly respected and admired by the general youth. At 3:00 PM, He Xiya first delivered an opening speech on behalf of Chairman Pan Gongzhan, and then the discussion began. The speakers spoke in the order of signing in. The majority opinions were summarized as follows: (1) Reading should focus on practical and useful learning. (2) Attention should be paid to physical health. (3) Young people should read more books related to physical and mental cultivation to stabilize their minds and absorb knowledge that meets the needs of the times, so as to cultivate sound talents to revive the nation. (4) History and geography are most important, law is most relevant to daily use, biographies of celebrities and great men are helpful for cultivating character, learning, and temperament, and natural science is the foundation of cultural history, so they should be read more. Newspapers are especially the place where citizens' common sense lies, so they should form a daily reading habit. (5) In addition to self-cultivation books, working youth should read more books related to their profession to increase their knowledge and skills. (6) Ancient books can be read slowly, but modern academics should be studied at present. (7) Toxic books, such as those about gods and monsters, pornography, and those whose theories are incompatible with the orthodox ideology of the country and the Three Principles of the People, should not be read, so as to avoid endless harm. (8) Reading should be economical and effective, so attention should be paid to methods, that is, selecting the subjects that are needed. For those related to enriching common sense, a broad approach is appropriate, that is, reading extensively. For those subjects that must be studied, a focused approach is appropriate, that is, reading intensively, and it is necessary to propose "self-centeredness" to avoid being aimless. It is also necessary to avoid "nearsightedness" and "astigmatism" in learning, so as to avoid superficiality and disorder. (9) In order to help the majority of those who cannot afford to study, it is appropriate to request the opening of public and private libraries to benefit students. More systematic academic lectures should be held, and more publications of the "Reading Guidance" type should be published. The publications can set up two columns, "Book Introduction" and "Academic Correspondence Q&A," in order to effectively take on the responsibility of guidance. It is best to have specialized scholars classify and review them accurately to introduce them, so as to reduce the energy and time of the majority of readers. The meeting adjourned at about 5:30 PM.

Results of the Preliminary Rounds of the Chinese Debate Competition Among Universities in East China: Fudan, Jinan, Hujiang, Central University, and Business College Win; Semifinals Will Be Held in Groups on May 4 181

This year, universities in East China held a Chinese debate competition according to the regulations. The participants included Central University, Jinling University, Ginling Women's College, Business College, Hujiang University, Fudan University, Jiaotong University, Jinan University, Southeast Medical College, and other schools. Economic Special Issue

Results of Gold and Silver Import and Export Statistics Over the Past Forty-Six Years: How Much Gold and Silver Does China Still Possess? 184

— Liu Tang

Since the price of gold became expensive and gold flowed out in torrents, and since the price of silver became expensive and silver flowed out in a continuous stream, the question of how much gold and silver China still holds is probably one that cannot be answered with certainty. Foreigners who do not understand our country's situation regard us as a silver-using country and harbor ulterior motives, thinking of using the means of raising the price of silver to fulfill their ambition of absorption and manipulation. Unscrupulous merchants and vagrants, seizing the opportunity, engage in smuggling and tax evasion, committing all kinds of evils. After enduring hardship, we have no other choice but to struggle hard. As for the situation of gold and silver inflows and outflows, which is closely related to us, we must examine it thoroughly.

The only figures that can be verified for gold and silver inflows and outflows are from customs records. However, according to the "Statistics of China's International Trade in the Past Sixty-Five Years," the customs report's statistical table of gold, silver, and copper imports and exports began in the twentieth year of the Guangxu reign (1904); before that, it was only mentioned in the reports. According to the statistical table, from the fifteenth year of the Guangxu reign (1889) to the seventeenth year of the Republic of China (1928), in these forty years, there were twenty-seven years with a gold surplus and twelve years with a deficit (the twenty-ninth year of the Guangxu reign, i.e., 1903, was balanced). For silver, from the sixteenth year of the Guangxu reign (1890) to the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, a total of thirty-nine years, there were twenty-five years with a surplus and fourteen years with a deficit. From this, it can be seen that there were more years with a gold surplus, while silver had more years with a surplus. The table below is a compilation of the annual surplus and deficit figures of gold (forty years) and silver (thirty-nine years) recorded in the statistical table, as well as the net value after offsetting the total surplus and deficit figures.

(Unit: Customs Taels)

Table 1: Net Amount of Gold and Silver Imports and Exports from the Fifteenth Year of Guangxu (Sixteenth Year for Silver) to the Seventeenth Year of the Republic of China.

Gold Surplus 200,761,920 Silver Surplus 194,931,612

Gold Deficit 104,001,703 Silver Deficit 822,109,039

Net Surplus 96,760,217 Net Deficit 627,177,427

If 1.5 is converted into silver dollars, the net gold surplus is worth 145,140,325 yuan, and the net silver deficit is 930,766,140 yuan. The difference is still a deficit of 785,625,815 yuan.

From the eighteenth year of the Republic of China (1929), the import and export figures for gold and silver are not included in the statistical table. According to the customs trade records, up to the twenty-second year of the Republic of China, the table is shown on the left:

(Unit: National Currency) Table 2: Net Amount of Gold and Silver Imports and Exports in the Five Years from the Eighteenth Year of the Republic of China

Gold Surplus 257,556,760 Silver Surplus 19,952,275

Gold Deficit None Silver Deficit 346,193,837

Net Surplus 257,556,760 Net Deficit 326,241,562

During these five years, the price of gold was very high, so there was a surplus every year. Silver, on the other hand, began to change to a surplus from the twenty-first year. Last year (the twenty-third year), under the influence of the American silver policy, the impact intensified. The huge surplus may also set a record unprecedented in history. However, the customs records for the twenty-third year have not yet been published. According to reports, the figures released by the customs are shown below.

Table 3: Net Amount of Gold and Silver Imports and Exports in the Twenty-Third Year of the Republic of China (1934) (Gold is calculated in Customs Gold Units, Silver is calculated in National Currency)

Gold Import 5,856 Silver Import 4,571,543

Gold Export 26,222,399 Silver Export 233,345,684

Surplus 26,216,543 Surplus 228,774,141

Looking at the above table, last year's gold and silver had a surplus. Gold was worth 26,216,523 Customs Gold Units, and silver was worth 228,774,141 yuan. Gold was almost entirely shipped to the United Kingdom, and silver also went to the United Kingdom the most, with 130 million yuan, the United States with 36 million yuan, and Japan with 10 million yuan. As for the situation in the first quarter of this year, according to reports, it is as follows:

Table 4: Net Amount of Gold and Silver Imports and Exports in the First Quarter of the Twenty-Fourth Year of the Republic of China (Units are the same as the above table)

Gold Import 76,666 Silver Import 3,596,500

Gold Export 13,969,110 Silver Export 100

Surplus 13,892,444 Deficit 3,596,400

The above-mentioned silver was all shipped from Hong Kong, the exported gold was shipped to the United Kingdom, and the imported gold came from Japan.

In the twenty-third year of the Republic of China, one Customs Gold Unit was approximately 1.9 National Currency Units. In the first quarter of this year, it was 1.799. Now, let us use 1.8 to convert the surplus value of gold for one year and one quarter into National Currency Units, totaling 72,196,141 yuan. Another table is compiled below:

Table 6: Net Amount of Gold and Silver Imports and Exports Over the Past Forty-Six Years (Forty-Five Years for Silver) (Unit: National Currency) From the Fifteenth Year of Guangxu (1889) to the First Quarter of the Twenty-Fourth Year of the Republic of China (1935)

Gold Surplus 630,895,781 Silver Surplus 541,123,834

Gold Deficit 156,002,554 Silver Deficit 1,582,953,795

Net Surplus 474,893,227 Net Deficit 1,041,829,961

In these forty-six years, gold had a deficit for only twelve years and a surplus for a total of thirty-three years. After offsetting the surplus and deficit, the surplus reached a huge value of 474,893,227 yuan. I am afraid that even if China has any gold reserves, they are already very few. Looking at the spot gold swap in April of this year, the final result was that the bulls had to pay in, which shows the scarcity of gold.

In these forty-five years, silver had a surplus for seventeen years and a deficit for twenty-eight years. After offsetting the surplus and deficit, the deficit still reached 1,041,829,961 yuan. If this is divided among the 440 million people, each person would only get about two yuan. Although the old silver reserves in China are not included, the small amount is already clearly visible. Why still arouse people's covetousness, wanting to force the Chinese people to have no gold or silver at all? Then China will certainly not be good, but will they also benefit?

New Trends in International Trade Deficits 185

— Yu Jieqiong

The deficit in international trade is a serious threat to China's economy. Without the accumulation of huge deficits over the years, the outflow of silver would not have been as turbulent and dangerous as it has been in the past year. Since the imposition of export duties on silver, silver has been temporarily detained in the country. However, if human efforts are relaxed even slightly, or if there are more drastic changes in the international market, the outflow of silver can occur at any time. For example, recently, the United States has once again raised the price of silver. Although our country's customs prohibitions are strict, the smuggling of silver in Tianjin, Xiamen, and other places still cannot be stopped. Furthermore, if the deficit phenomenon is not eliminated, even if silver exports stop due to taxation, there will eventually be a need to transport cash for export sooner or later in order to balance the trade deficit. Therefore, those who discuss China's financial problems in recent times invariably seek the root cause and focus on the trade deficit that has persisted for years.

The trade deficit is an important crux of the current deteriorating financial and economic situation and a tool for imperialists to control China's finance and economy. To break the current precarious financial and economic situation and to remove the superior control of foreigners, eliminating the deficit is the most important task at present. Therefore, the steps and methods to be taken are issues that we should study. This article is willing to explain the recent trends in international trade deficits based on facts, so that the Chinese people can have a deeper understanding of this important issue.

In the past two years, the value of the deficit has gradually decreased. This is something that everyone knows, and the degree of reduction is very rapid. Not only is the absolute value of the deficit declining rapidly, but the relative value is also declining rapidly. Let us look at the following facts. (Unit: Thousand Yuan)

1931 1933 1935

Deficit Value in Three Years 877,168 733,146 494,451

Percentage of Deficit Value to Total Trade Volume 36.0% 37.5% 31.6%

The first line represents the absolute value. Last year's deficit was 380 million yuan less than the highest record in 1932 and 240 million yuan less than in 1933. The amount cannot be said to be insignificant. The second line represents the relative value. We know that in recent years, the total value of our country's trade has been declining rapidly, and the decline in the deficit is even faster, especially last year. In 1933, the deficit accounted for 37.5% of the total trade value, while last year it only accounted for 31.6%. This shows that the reduction in the deficit is faster than the reduction in the total trade volume.

However, what has been said above is still the surface value. What about the real exports and imports (i.e., the exports and imports of goods)? To understand the trend of the real deficit more clearly, we must further analyze it.

The trade volume we usually speak of refers to the value of the goods traded, and the deficit amount refers to the numerical value of the deficit, not the quantity of goods. The value of goods is the result of multiplying the quantity of goods by the price. Truly, to understand the trend of the deficit, we must eliminate the changes in prices to observe the situation of real quantity moving in and out. The following table observes the changes in quantity after eliminating prices. The result of dividing the export and import values by the export and import price indices can represent the trend of quantity. The result of dividing the value index by the price index is the quantity index. The last line is the situation of quantity inflow and outflow with 1926 as the base year. The reason why it should be marked with 1926 as the base year is because we are using the index with 1926 as the base period.

1932 1933 1934

(1) Import Value (Unit: Thousand Yuan, same below) 1,63,073 1,343,668 919,663

(2) Import Value Index (1926 as base period, same below) 93.3 76.8 53.1

(3) Import Price Index 140.2 132.2 132.0

(4) Quantity after eliminating price changes (i.e., dividing 1 by 3) 1,164,816 1,015,622 704,296

(5) Import Quantity Index (i.e., dividing 2 by 3) 66.6 58.1 40.2

(6) Export Value 765,956 611,822 535,32

(7) Value Index 57.0 45.4 39.8

(8) Export Price Index 90.4 82.0 71.7

(9) Quantity after eliminating prices (i.e., dividing 6 by 8) 847,197 746,124 746,460

(10) Export Quantity Index (i.e., dividing 7 by 8) 73.1 55.3 55.5

(11) Quantity Inflow and Outflow with 1926 as the Calculation Base (10) Deficit (11) Surplus 37,519 (10) 369,498 (11) 42,170

This table shows several important facts. First, the import price last year was not much different from the previous year, but the import value last year declined significantly. This shows that all the reduction was in quantity. This is very obvious. The value of goods is obtained by multiplying the price by the quantity. If the value of goods decreases significantly while the price remains unchanged, it is sufficient to show that what has changed is completely the third number, that is, the quantity. Second, the export quantity last year not only did not decrease compared to the previous year, but even increased slightly. This can be seen from the export quantity index. The index for the previous year was 55.3, while last year it was 55.5, an increase of 0.2. However, the export value last year also decreased. Since there was no decline in quantity, the reason for the decrease in value must be entirely due to changes in price.

This is a very noteworthy fact. On the import side last year, the price did not change, and what decreased was the import quantity. On the export side last year, the quantity did not change, and what decreased was only the price. Therefore, after eliminating the changes in prices, the export and import quantities are seen to be closer to each other. In other words, the real quantity deficit is far less than what is expressed on the value of goods.

Secondly, we compare the export and import values after eliminating the changes in prices. If we take 1926 as the calculation benchmark, last year's quantity was no longer a deficit, but a surplus.

Therefore, we have arrived at a very important conclusion here, namely, that the deficit value in recent times has gradually decreased, and in fact, the quantity deficit is even smaller. The large decline in the trade value last year was entirely due to the decrease in the quantity of imports. As for the import prices, there was no decline. On the export side, the reason for the decline was entirely due to the drop in export prices. As for the export quantity, it not only did not decrease last year, but even increased slightly.

Why does this phenomenon occur? We should explain it. Last year, due to the rise in the price of silver, our country's currency increased in value invisibly. Logically, foreign goods imported into our country, calculated in our currency, should have seen their prices fall. That is to say, the price of imports must have fallen. The main reason why they did not fall is that the prices in various countries gradually rose last year, which was enough to offset the price drop in our market. Therefore, last year's import prices did not fall further. As for the sudden decline in the quantity of imports, it was the result of the extreme decline in the purchasing power of the people. They simply did not have the ability to buy, which caused a very large decline in the quantity of imports. As for the export side, the reason why the export quantity was able to stop declining was partly due to the fact that the world's economic situation turned to prosperity, and the demand for our country's goods showed an increase. Another reason was that exporters tried their best to lower export prices in order to survive by any means. The very large drop in export prices last year was partly due to this point, and another reason was due to the currency devaluation policies of various countries. Because of the devaluation of currencies in various countries, our goods, after being transported to foreign countries, were priced in foreign currencies, and the prices increased invisibly, making them impossible to sell. In order to maintain their businesses, exporters had no choice but to drastically lower export prices. This is the most important reason for the crazy drop in export prices last year.

The above is an explanation of the conclusions we obtained earlier. What will the situation be like in the future? This is what we should also speculate on in this article.

According to the results of our analysis, the reduction in imports in recent years is entirely due to the reduction in the quantity of imports. There has not been much change in the price. Therefore, the reduction in the deficit in recent years is entirely due to the reduction in the quantity of imported goods. The reason for this is that the people do not have the ability to buy. We speculate that within a considerable period of time, there is no reason for the purchasing power of the people to increase out of thin air, because judging from the current situation, the national economy is on the road to fragmentation, and it is natural that the purchasing power of the people will decrease day by day. As the purchasing power of the people decreases day by day, the quantity of foreign goods needed will also decrease day by day. Therefore, the future import value has a tendency to decrease again. As for the export side, because the world market has improved, and the demand for our country's goods may increase, it seems that the quantity of our country's exports has the hope of rebounding with the recovery of the world economy. As for export prices, it is temporarily impossible to recover and rise due to the pressure of the currency policies of various countries. From this, we believe that imports have the possibility of decreasing again, and exports seem to have the hope of rebounding. Therefore, it is highly probable that the deficit amount will decrease again.

In summary, the trade deficit value has been decreasing day by day in recent years, and the quantity deficit after eliminating price changes has decreased even more. The decline in imports last year was entirely due to the shortage of quantity, while the decline in exports was entirely due to the drop in prices. The purely quantity deficit is in fact much lower than the deficit expressed by the numerical value, and the future trend is that the deficit amount is expected to fall again. This is the conclusion we have reached through analysis.

However, the reduction in the deficit amount does not mean that we can be optimistic. We must not forget that this is the result of the people's poverty and oppression. And we must not think that because the deficit has decreased, the deficit will no longer be a problem in the future. Today, the people's ability to bear the burden is far from what it used to be. Although today's deficit amount is decreasing very rapidly, the decline in the people's ability to bear the burden is even faster. In comparison, the people's deficit burden is still becoming heavier day by day. The deficit is still an important issue at present and does not lose its importance due to the reduction in the amount. How to solve it still needs to be studied. What has been said above is only a report on the real trend of the deficit.

New Ways to Develop Export Trade 186

— Kong Dian

I.

In recent years, China's foreign trade has suffered a sharp decline in exports, leading to a dramatic increase in the deficit, and the outflow of cash has been endless. If this continues, the national economy will undoubtedly wither and decline. Some people in the current era are discussing the idea of organizing export credit insurance to develop future foreign trade. Therefore, I will briefly describe its outline as follows:

Export credit insurance is a special system aimed at filling the risks of export credit. In detail, it means that if the foreign importer who is the payer of the draft issued by the exporter for collecting goods goes bankrupt or refuses to pay, the insurance industry, as a third party, will bear a certain amount of compensation to the issuer or the discount bank. The so-called export risks can be analyzed into two types:

First, those who are unable to pay. The reasons for this can be divided into bankruptcy and extraordinary incidents.

(1) The risk caused by bankruptcy is called bankruptcy risk. It is mostly caused by the bankruptcy of the buyer. For the benefit of the exporter, if there is no third party to provide protection for this kind of occasional and unavoidable fact, there will inevitably be concerns about the operation of international trade, and they will not dare to boldly do it. Therefore, the content of export credit insurance at the beginning mostly focused on underwriting this kind of risk as its main business. As for what kind of state is called bankruptcy, ordinary laws have detailed regulations. As long as this kind of provision is stated in the insurance policy, it can be used as the key to solving problems in the future. Also, even if the buyer has not reached bankruptcy, but his financial situation is on the verge of desperation, and he has to announce the clearing of accounts, so that all or part of the debt cannot be paid, it can be regarded as quasi-bankruptcy. It should be stipulated in the insurance policy that the policyholder can transfer the continuation of the debt entrustment (Abandonment) to the insurer and obtain its compensation.

(2) When the foreign importer of the buyer is unable to perform his debts due to war, floods, earthquakes, and government issuance of payment extension orders, it is called extraordinary risk (Catastropherrik). If importers are caught in a whirlpool, they will inevitably be unable to get rid of it and fall into a desperate situation of bankruptcy, transferring their losses to the exporter without a doubt. However, although relying on insurance is extremely important, ordinary credit insurance companies are usually exempt from their responsibilities for the occurrence of irresistible accidents. Therefore, whether the underwriting of extraordinary risks should be done by the power of the state has become a problem.

Second, those who refuse to pay. The reasons for refusing to pay may be due to poor quality or late delivery, resulting in the buyer's unwillingness to pick up the goods, or due to the drop in the price of goods or the tight money supply, the inability to transfer the payment, and the desire to return the goods, resulting in the refusal to accept the draft. Although the former cannot be used as the purpose of concluding an insurance contract, it is not easy to predict the risk of the latter, unless the reason for its occurrence can be attributed to the buyer. In general, it is not included in the scope of underwriting.

II.

From the perspective of private economy, the most effective strategy in export trade is to meet the hopes of overseas customers in general trading conditions such as goods, prices, and payment methods, and to be better than other competitors. If this can be done, then without solicitation, people will scramble to inquire in order to achieve the success of their transactions. However, whether the quality and price of goods can be better and cheaper is always governed by various conditions, and it is not easy to achieve overnight. However, the method of payment can be changed artificially. For example, if the payment for goods has always been short-term, it can now be changed to long-term, or documentary bills. If the buyer is required to pay the goods before handing them over (Documents against payment) (referred to as Dp), it can now be changed to Documents against acceptance (referred to as DA). The buyer only needs to promise to pay the amount stated on the bill in the future, and it will be handed over to him, so that after the goods are picked up, he can engage in selling them on the one hand and returning the goods on the other. Since there is no inconvenience of temporarily raising funds to purchase goods, who would not want to purchase their goods and be happy to promote them. However, if this is followed, not to mention that exporters have limited capital and are unable to engage in this long-term credit sale, the risks they bear are very large. If the buyer encounters other reasons during this period, resulting in the declaration of bankruptcy, or even using other reasons to delay payment, who can bear this as a profit-making trader. This is in terms of the exporter. The importance of export credit insurance is so great. (To be continued)

Securities: The Bond Market Was Stagnant Last Week 188

Last week, from April 15th to 20th, at the Chinese Securities Exchange, as the April futures delivery approached, both the bulls and bears maintained a firm defensive posture. Their lines remained unmoved, without either side attempting to crush the other, nor were there any hurried swap transactions. The market situation was almost numb, and the morale of investors was increasingly scattered. Arbitrageurs saw meager profits, so they were not enthusiastic. Speculators found no opportunities to exploit, so they mostly stayed on the sidelines. Superficially, due to the loosening of credit by the three banks and the financial accommodations from the "four bottoms" (referring to basic industries), there seemed to be hope for a slight recovery in finance and commerce. However, in reality, the special increase in American silver prices had a significant impact. Talk of a British pound loan seemed like a mirage, desirable but unattainable. Only the government's efforts to rescue the financial situation were highly active. In the near future, there should be a clear demonstration of progress. The public bond market, in this uncertain and confusing period, was also caught in a chaotic and swirling pattern. Regarding the 96 Public Bonds, it was rumored that certain prominent figures ("鉅公") were unable to cover their large short positions, so there were initial rumors of it not being listed on the exchange, followed by rumors of old bonds being universally accepted. All sorts of news were unfavorable for the bulls. One side was trying to suppress the price, so the future outlook must still show some decline. Due to the large short positions that were not covered, prices will ultimately be unable to rise. The week progressed with a weak market on Monday after settlement, with minimal fluctuations. On Tuesday, due to the surge in American silver, floating long positions emerged, resulting in a small gain of about half a yuan. On Wednesday, there was some short-covering and swapping, recovering about half a yuan. From Thursday to Saturday, the situation was extremely chaotic, with stagnant trading, and no significant fluctuations occurred even as the delivery date approached. Only the 96 Public Bonds saw a sudden increase in trading volume due to various rumors, and a downward trend gradually began. The future situation, having been brewing for too long, is such that if a slight crack appears, there will inevitably be a surge. Overall, the week's market price results showed that fluctuations were only one or two jiao (tenths of a yuan), with declines generally outnumbering gains. The total transaction volume was 59,959,500 yuan, plus 7,000 yuan in spot transactions. Free Talk

On Poetry 193

— Jiang Jiping

Suiyuan Shihua discusses the need for poetry to be "winding," which is similar to Wang Guowei's concept of "unconstrained." However, I believe that when writing poetry, one might as well be nosy and foolish. For example, "The sound of wind and rain came last night; who knows how many flowers have fallen" is being nosy, but it is done well. Another example is Chen Chunan's inscription on a painting of a beautiful woman's back:

"The beauty leans against a jade闽干 (railing), regretting that her beautiful face is hard to see; I call out to her several times, but she doesn't turn around; with foolish heart, I want to turn the painting around to see."

The merit lies in knowingly being a painting, but still wanting to turn it around to see. This is foolish, but this foolishness is a poetic foolishness.

There is a section in Suiyuan Shihua discussing the winding nature of poetry, which can greatly inspire one's spirit. It says, "Someone asked, 'How can poetry be considered winding?' I replied: 'There are countless examples of winding ancient poetry. For example, the recent poem by Wang Ziyuan visiting a friend says: 'Restless crows settle down at the third watch of the night, a single silver lamp shines brightly upstairs; I remember arriving at the door but not knocking, quietly listening to the sound of reading in the flower shade.' This is winding. If he had knocked upon arriving at the door, it would have been straightforward. Fang Mengzhang's poem visiting a friend says: 'A light boat winds through misty clouds, I love even more the flowers filling the valleys before the mountain; not only am I not seeking you, I also linger, not knowing your home is within the flowers.' This is winding. If he had known it was 君家 (your home) from the start, it would have been straightforward. A Song dynasty poem about plum blossoms says: 'Green willows, understanding language, should laugh at each other, who exactly leaked the spring light?' A poem about red plum blossoms says: 'A shepherd boy wakes up with drowsy eyes, mistakenly recognizing the peach grove, wanting to release the cattle.' Thinking of the heart of willows and the eyes of shepherd boy when writing about plum blossoms is winding. If it only focused on plum blossoms, it would be straightforward.'"

What is meant by "winding" is having a different and beautiful realm in the poem, something that others would not think of. It is as if one has reached the source of a stream, and the road ahead is blocked by a mountain, as if "this road leads nowhere," but suddenly turning around, going around the mountain, there is a sudden opening, with many beautiful sights that one cannot take in at a glance. At this time, the person reading the poem naturally receives a kind of joy. This is what is meant by "unconstrained," "winding," "having divine charm," "spirit," and "humor." Whatever one calls it is fine. Good poems have no difference; whether it is new poetry or old poetry, criticism of poetry cannot deviate from the above ways of expression.

Poetry is something that should be written when one is moved. If someone gives a topic, there will definitely be no masterpieces. If we open Tang poetry to look, is there even one good poem written in response to imperial command? Yuan Zicai said: "Poems without titles are the music of heaven; poems with titles are the music of man. The music of heaven is easy to achieve, while the music of man is difficult. The three hundred poems of the Book of Songs and the Nineteen Old Poems are all works without titles. Later people took the first one or two characters from the poem and made it the title, thus making them uniquely outstanding for thousands of years. From the Han and Wei dynasties onward, poetry only had titles, and emotions gradually weakened. By the Tang dynasty, there were five-character eight-rhyme examination poems limited by rules and regulations, and emotions became even more distant." What is meant by having poetry without a title is that the emotion must be at its peak. Poems written in this way must be works of spirit. I believe that writing poetry is like making friends. Two good friends get together, sit knee to knee, and pour out their hearts. They feel that every word and sentence they say to each other is very touching, and every sentence is filled with rich emotions. Even if they talk until late at night, they show no signs of weariness. Writing poetry when we are moved is also like this. Sometimes, waking up in the winter night, hearing several desolate and clear clapper sounds outside, or on a clear spring morning, seeing the willow branches on the riverbank swaying in the wind, suddenly, one's heart stirs, and the poetic lines in one's chest seem like the rolling river water about to flow out of the embankment. It is truly unpleasant not to pour them out. This is when the spirit arrives. If one writes poetry without being moved, it is like dealing with a disliked friend. The more one dislikes them, the more one feels there is nothing to say. Even if one can say a few words, they are perfunctory words that are irrelevant. Both feel bored and wish they could quickly get away. Hardship in writing is like this. One sits at the desk, pen in hand, unable to find half a sentence. One walks around the walls and flips through books, but also gains nothing. Writing poetry in this way is truly a torture of life. Jia Dao, a famous hardship poet of the Tang dynasty, had a line saying:

"Two lines take three years to obtain, one sigh brings forth tears; if the appreciator

does not admire them, I will return to sleep in the old mountains in autumn."

He first misunderstood the purpose of writing poetry. The ancients said, "Poetry expresses intention." What is meant by "expressing intention" is expressing one's own emotions and saying what one wants to say. Whether others appreciate it or not is their business, what does it have to do with me? For the sake of others' appreciation, refusing to say one's own words is destroying one's spirit and will definitely not produce good lines. No wonder it takes him "three years to obtain two lines." Looking at the poems of the ancients, those who can express their own opinions all have their own individuality, not echoing what others say. In fact, things are already outdated, but after being described by his pen and expressing his unique opinion, they can still shine brightly. This is the benefit of being able to say one's own words. For example, Li Bai's poem "If only Guan Zhong were always alive, why not have six more ladies in the palace!" Yang Chengzhai's poem says, "I only wish the monarch would execute Zai Pi, not worrying about Xi Shi in the palace." A Tang dynasty poem praising Emperor Minghuang says, "If Yao and Song had not lost the imperial concubine, how could the barbarian dust have reached China!" Emperor Xizong's poem when fleeing to Shu says, "Aman (Cao Cao) in the underworld should have something to say, this time he should no longer blame Yang Guifei." Fan Tongshu's poem says, "If the prime minister of Wu were still here, the King of Yue would have sent the beauty in vain." A Tang dynasty poem says, "The King of Wu did everything upside down, Xi Shi may not be superior to the six palace ladies." These poems all have their own opinions, not relying on the ancients, so they are exceptionally novel. Some people may clearly have this kind of opinion, but they dare not say it, that is still being unwilling to say their own words.

Night Talk on a Boat 194

— Tang Xiru

I took the last scheduled steamer from Wuxi to go home. I heard that there wouldn't be any more tomorrow, because the river water was too shallow. Not only were the farmers along the way opposed to the operation of the steamers (because it could easily damage the dragon-bone water lifts), but even the petty-minded steamer owners were advocating suspending the service. Because even if the boat was running slowly, as slow as a snail crawling, they still had to be careful all the time that there weren't any rocks on the riverbed that would bite off a piece of the bottom of the boat.

From sunrise to sunset, I barely managed to endure until Heqiao. From here to my home, there were still more than twenty li of waterway, but the steamer didn't go along this route, so I had to hire a rowboat.

This time, my father had hired a boat from our hometown to pick me up, so I was spared a lot of trouble. I walked across the gangplank of the steamer in the fine rain, stepped onto the gangplank of the rowboat, and asked the boatman to go ashore to buy some noodles and porridge to fill our stomachs. Then the boat immediately set off again in the dense darkness of the night.

I hadn't been back for seven or eight years, so my father was busy telling me about the changes in our hometown over the years. Who had died, who had taken up opium, what shops had closed down. Who had joined the Green Gang and even become a leader, with as many as two or three hundred disciples, rampaging through the area. All were trivial news, gray news, news that was both surprising and stifling.

The boat rowed less than three li out of Heqiao Town, and the boat window immediately became lively and bright. Torches, safety lamps, lanterns. So many on both sides of the bank that they looked like stars. The wheezing of the water pumps, the dry howling of the dragon-bone water lifts, the shouts of the farmers, the frenzied barking of the village dogs, and the shadowy figures coming and going all combined to compose a piece of music that made one want to commit suicide, and formed a picture that made one want to weep. The more desperately they struggled, the more they showed their greatness, and at the same time, how bitter and pitiful they were!

The lights faded away, and the sounds also faded away. We had already reached the famous large river in the area. The villagers here seemed to depend entirely on the bounty of this river, and now they could rest at night. All around was quiet, and the moonlight came out, illuminating clumps of tree shadows and blocks of dark roof shadows, sleeping wearily. If it weren't for the wheat-like reality we had just encountered, this would have been the most ideal moonlit night scene like a lyrical poem. But....

"Damn you! Are you asleep? Row to the middle of the river! Do you want to run aground on the shoal? There was a loud scolding from someone in the stern, and at the same time, there was the sound of a bamboo pole poking into the water from the bow of the boat.

I had been listening to the tired creaking of the oars for so long that I was almost asleep.

Suddenly, my father leaned out of the window, knocked the soot out of his pipe on the windowsill, cleared his throat, and said, "We're almost there! Let's go to the bow of the boat to clear our heads."

We went to the bow of the boat and sat down. Suddenly, my father said to me in a low voice, "That...that's it in front of us, on the riverbank to the left. There's a white coffin. That's the policeman who was beaten to death by the hooligans.... They tricked him into going out to catch gamblers and beat him to death.... What a pity! He wasn't even twenty-eight years old yet..."

After saying that, my father stood up, turned his back to the left, muttered the words "The wronged have their avengers, the debtors have their creditors," cleared his throat again, deliberately coughed a few times, and loudly addressed the boatman:

"Jinlong, there are a few black clouds in the southwest corner! It's going to be a downpour tomorrow."

"I hope so! Amitabha! If God doesn't have mercy again, the poor will have no food to eat!"

Mountain Pastoral (1) 195

— Ai Wu

"Let's rest, everyone, let's rest! ...It's so hot!"

The man called Boss Qin by his companion stopped and took a breath. While lifting his right foot to loosen the area where his straw sandals had rubbed and caused pain, he anxiously shouted loudly to the people who had walked to the other side of the slope. Old Xu, carrying a load of sundries such as foreign thread and needles, immediately stopped, wiped the sweat from his forehead, and said:

"Okay, let's wait for him!"

"Don't mind him, let him suffer a little! ...He's putting on the airs of a big boss here! ...Keep going."

Old Chen turned around and said this, while shrugging the blue cloth bundle on his back, and continued walking forward.

Old Xu smiled, agreed, and shifted the load on his left shoulder to his right, following behind.

Seeing that no one on the other side of the slope responded, Boss Qin thought to himself: These two fellows aren't going to wait for me? He wanted to sit down and rest, but since setting off in the morning, he hadn't seen a single house, and this hillside was full of low evergreen bushes, quiet as if he had entered a primeval forest. He couldn't help but feel afraid and had to endure the pain in his feet and walk forward.

The season was subtropical spring. The miscellaneous trees on the hilltop and in the ditches were all sprouting new buds in their perennial greenness, emitting a light bitter taste and fragrance. Along the way, the leaves were flashing with spots of golden sunlight. There was no wind, and everywhere was sweltering.

Turning past the slope, seeing the backs of the two men walking slowly, Old Qin called out again:

"Hey, don't you two feel heavy? ...It's so hot! ...It's okay for me to be empty-handed!"

"It's okay! It's okay!"

Old Chen turned his head and replied loudly, then turned back and continued walking, smiling gleefully as he whispered to Old Xu:

"Damn, he's saying it's okay for him! Look!"

"Brother Xu, aren't you resting either? ...Just focusing on the road will make you feel heart-stricken! Carrying such a heavy load."

Boss Qin persuaded Old Xu alone. Old Chen whispered:

"Look, he's trying to ingratiate himself with you, don't mind him. He thinks of us all as laborers, bah!"

Old Xu felt it was wrong to ignore others, but he didn't want to stop obediently, so he shifted the load on his shoulder and replied loudly:

"Boss Qin, let's walk a little further before resting, there's no water to drink here!"

Old Chen sarcastically smiled quietly:

"You're the only one who likes to call him boss! ...What boss? He's simply unreliable!"

Above the Tower, Below the Tower 196

— Ben Shui

As the distance lessened, the Xishan Pagoda grew larger in our eyes.

We followed the winding stone steps up the mountain, up the temple. We followed the ancient, dim stairs up the tower, up to the top of the tower.

As the stairs rose higher, the wind grew stronger. A blade of grass, a tree on the top of the mountain, were all moving.

I used my two eyes to look down, to look at everything. I knew that the whole city was so big, so wide, but now it all rushed into my eyes. I could count clearly this building and that building. I knew that a blade of grass on the top of Huishan, a wave in Taihu Lake, a line of people on the mountain path, a car on the road were all moving, all moving. But in my eyes, they had all become solidified things.

I looked at the many mountains like many graves, looked at Taihu Lake like a pond, looked at a six-foot-tall person like a child in a land of little people, looked at the cars and horses like toys.

"Ha, ha, they are all insignificant in my eyes."

I also knew that the society we were in now was a tower, and I was on the top of the tower, so undoubtedly I was the master of this tower. Ha, ha, millions of people are under my feet, under my feet! I kicked my foot on the cement ground, ringing.

I casually threw a remaining cigarette butt down, and it stumbled and rolled in the wind like a drunkard for a long time before landing.

I spat a little saliva casually, and it also stumbled and rolled down.

"Ah, a cigarette butt and a little saliva on the top of the tower also become great!"

My face was glowing.

Dusk urged us down the tower, and we stepped on the winding stone steps again. I knew that the people on the tower at this time were looking at us as insignificant; but when I looked back at the people left on the tower, I also felt that they were insignificant. No, even the tower itself I felt was insignificant. No, even Xishan, I felt was insignificant at all.

A nameless melancholy piled up in my heart.

As the distance increased, the Xishan Pagoda disappeared from our sight.

Dance Marathon 197

— (By American J.T. Farrell, Translated by Yi Xian)

— Sketches of American Life —

Tax Fellers was originally a strong shepherd boy from the mountainous region of Greece. His hard-working mother saved up some money, enough to make a trip to America, a country where, according to everyone, the streets are paved with gold, there are grand buildings everywhere, women dress like princesses, men's pockets are full of money, every boy has a bicycle, every man and woman owns a car, and all the houses are like palaces. Tax was tall and strong, and at the age of thirteen, looking older than his age, he arrived in a city in this heaven called Chicago.

As this frightened child sat on the train, a relative came to meet him. This relative took him to their home on South Halsted Street and told him to work in a candy store. Soon, Tax discovered the meaning of life in heaven. It meant working from six in the morning until six in the evening, and even later on Saturdays and Sundays. It meant sweeping the store, washing dishes, wiping doors, cleaning equipment, tidying up, and running errands. It meant attending night school to learn English when his eyes could barely stay open, and constantly being laughed at for not making progress. It meant walking and living in dirty streets, constantly bombarded by the gas, dust, soot, and exhaust fumes from cars, causing him to cough. It meant that whenever he thought of his hometown in the Greek mountains, his mother, and the leisurely days of shepherding, he was overcome with deep loneliness.

For many days after starting at the store, Tax remained a very quiet child. He always thought back to his hometown and the games he played with other children, and he remembered his old mother's smile and kisses. He feared everything about America, the chaotic heavenly life of Chicago. He patiently worked every day, saving five dollars a week, pinching pennies from it to deposit in an immigrant bank. However, he hoped that one day he would become just like an American, speak the same language as them, wear the clothes they wore, ride in cars like them, and take American girls out.

Gradually, Tax learned all sorts of tricks. He learned to speak American, but he couldn't learn to speak it like an American. He realized that he was an unrefined Greek peasant, and many Americans didn't want him or his many compatriots to come to America. He learned that American girls laughed at young Greek peasants. Moreover, he also discovered some places where he could go for two dollars to find American girls who wouldn't laugh at Greek peasants, and he could have fun for at least five or ten cents. He learned when he could buy cheap American clothes, how to wear purple silk shirts and purple socks, and how to tie an orange tie. Gradually, he also learned that he could pocket some of the money he put into the cash register at the store.

Later, the relative who employed him became enraged and fired him, calling him a thief and an ungrateful wretch. Tax was somewhat indignant and retorted that he had made a lot of money selling this shoddy merchandise, and yet he only paid him six dollars a week.

Later, Tax was employed by other compatriots, working in fruit stores, soda fountains, bars, and restaurants. He became increasingly familiar with American society and the American language. Sometimes, he would wear a purple silk shirt and matching socks, tie an orange tie, and stroll in the park or along South Halsted Street, hoping to find a beautiful, pink-skinned, blue-eyed American girl for himself. Sometimes, he would think of his Greek mountain village, dreaming of returning there with American money, and also bringing a girl, perhaps one of these rosy-skinned, young, and beautiful American girls.

Tax spent many years drifting along. He was in his twenties and still carried his original residence permit. He had always worked like a dog, and he continued to do the same odd jobs he had been doing since he came to America. He earned fifteen dollars a week, working twelve hours a day in a candy store. He swept, wiped, scrubbed, tidied, and served customers. Whenever he got a chance, he would pocket some money from the cash register. Every week, he went to the bank to deposit money. He checked his bankbook almost every night, pleased to see his savings grow. However, he could never save up much money, because he often had to take time off work, and then he had to live off his savings until he found a new job.
